fful pale he was fordrunke and not red
He ȝyksneth and spekyth þourw þe nose
As he were on þe quakke or on þe pose
To bedde he goþ and with hym goth his wif
As ony iay sche lyȝt was and iolyf
So was here ioly whistele wel Iwet
The cradil at here beddys feet is set
To rokke and to ȝeue þe child to souke
And whan þat dronkyn al was in þe crouke
To bedde wente þe douȝtyr ryȝt anon
To bedde goth aleyn and ek Iohn
Ther nas no mor hem neded no dwale
This mellere hath so wysely bibbit alle
That as an hors he snortyth in hese slep
Ne of hese tayl ne takyth he no kep
Hese wif bar hym a burdoun a ful strong
Men myȝtyn here hyre route too furlong
The wenche routyth ek par cumpaynye
Aleyn þe clerk þat herde þis melodye


He pokede ion and seyde slepist þou
Herdist þou euere swich a song er now
Lo swich a copil is among hem alle
A wylde fyr mote on here bodyis falle
Ho herkenyth euere swich a ferly thyng  
Ȝa þey schal haue þe flour of ille endyng
This longe nyȝt þere tydis me no reste
But ȝit no fors al schal ben for the beste
ffor Iohn seyde he as euere mote I thryue
Ȝif þat I may þe wenche wele I schryue
Sum esement has lawe Ischapyn vs
ffor Iohn þere is a lawe þat says þus
That ȝif a man in a poynt be agreuyd
That in a noþer he schal ben releuyd
Oure corn is stolin schortly it is non nay
And we han had an ille fit al þis day
And syn I schal han non amendement
Ageyn my los I wele haue eysement
By godys sale it schal non oþer be
This Iohn answerde Aley avise þe
The mellere is a perlyous man he seyde
And ȝif þat he out of hese slep abreyde
He myȝte vs don bothe a velanye
Alyn answerde I counte hym not a flye
And vp he sterte and by þe wenche he crepte
This wenche lay vp ryght and faste slepte
Tyl he so nygh was er sche myghte aspye
That it hadde be to late for to crye
And schortely for to seyn þey were at on
Now pley aleyn for I wele speke of ion
This Iohn lyth stylle a furlong wey or too
And to hym self he makyth reuthe and woo
Allas quod he þis is a wekede iape
Now may I seyn þat I is but an ape
Ȝit hath myn felawe sumwhat for hese harm
He has þe melleris douȝtyr in hese arm


He auntered hym and has hese nedis sped
And I lye as a draf sek in myn bed
And whan þis iape is told a noþer day
I schal ben told a daffe a cokenay
I wele ryse and antere it be myn fay  
Vnhardi is vnsely þus men say
And vp he ros and softely he wente
Vn to þe cradil and in hese hond it hente
And bar it softe vn to hese bedis feet
Sone aftyr þis þe wyf here routyng let
And gan to wake and lefte for to pysse
And cam ageyn and gan here cradil mysse
And gropede here and þere  but sche fond non
Allas quod sche I hadde almost mys gon
I hadde al most gon to þe clerkys bed
Ey benedyste þanne hadde I foule Isped
And forth sche goth tyl sche þe cradel fond
Sche gropede alwey ferþere with here hond
And fond þe bed and thouȝte not but good
Be cause þat þe cradyl by it stod
And nyste where sche was for it was derk
And fayre and wel sche crep in bi þe clerk
And lyth ful stylle and wolde a cauȝt a slep
Withinne a while þis Iohn vp lep
And on þis goode wif he leyth on sore
So merye a fit ne hadde sche ful ȝore
He prikyth harde and sore as he were mad
This ioly lyf han þese too klerkis lad
Tyl þat þe fyrste kok began to synge
Aleyn wex wery in þe dawenynge
ffor he hadde swonkyn al þe longe nyȝt
And seyde farwel malyn swete wyȝt
The day is come I may no lengere byde
But euere more where so I go or ryde
I is þyn owene clerk so haue I sel
Now dere leman quod sche go fare weel


But er þou go on thyng I wele þe telle
Whan þat þou wendyst homward be þe melle
Ryȝt at þe entre of þe dore behynde  
Þou schat a cake of half a buschel fynde
Þat was Imakyd ryȝt of þyn owene mele
Which þat I halp myn fadyr for to stele
And goode leman god þe saue and kepe
And with þat word sche gan almost to wepe
Aleyn vp ryst and thoughte er þan it dawe
I wele gon crepe in by myn felawe
And fond þe cradyl with hese hand anon
By god þouȝte he al wrong I haue mys gon
Myn hed is toty of myn swynk to nyȝt
Þat makyth me þat I go not aryȝt
I wot wel by þe cradyl I haue mys go
Here lyth þe mellere and hese wyf also
And forth he goth a twenty deleway
Vn to þe bed þere þat þe mellere lay
He wende a crepid bi hese felawe Ion
An by þe mellere in he crepede anon
And cauȝte hym by þe nekke softe he spak
He seyde þou Iohn þou sweuenyst awak
ffor cristis soule and here a nobele game
ffor by þat lord þat called is seynt Iame
As I haue thryes in þe schorte nyȝt
Swyuyd þe melleris douȝtyr bolt vp ryȝt
Whil þou hast as a coward been agast
Ȝa false harlot quod þe mellere hast
A false traytour false clerk quod he
Thow schat ben ded be godis dynete
Ho durste ben so bold to disparage
Myn douȝtyr þat is comyn of swych lenage
And by the throte bolle he caughte aleyn
And he hente hym dyspitously ageyn
And on þe nose he smot hym with hese fest
Doun ran þe blod strem vp on hese brest


And in þe floor with nose and mouth tobroke
They walwe as don too piggis in a poke
And vp þey gon and don ageyn anon  
Tyl þat þe mellere spurnede aȝen a ston
And doun he fyl bakward vp on hese wif
That wiste no þyng of þis nyse stryf
ffor sche was falle a slepe a lyte wyght
With Iohn þe clerk þat wakede al nyȝt
And with þe fal out of here slep sche bryde
Help holy croys of bromeholm sche seyde
In manus tuas lord to þe I calle
Awake symond þe fend is on vs falle
Myn herte is brokyn allas I ne am but ded
There lyth on vp on myn wombe and on myn hed
Help symkyn for þe false klerkys fyȝte
This Iohn styrte vp as faste as euere he myȝte
And graspith by the walle to and fra
To fynde a staf and sche styrte vp alswa
And knew þe estis betere þan dede þis Iohn
And bi þe wal a staf sche fond anon
And saw a lytyl schemeryng of a lyȝt
ffor at an hole in schon þe mone bryt
And by þat lyȝt sche say hem boþe too
But sekyrly sche nyste ho was who
But as sche say a whit thyng in here eye
And whan sche gan þe whyte þyng espye
Sche wende þe clerk hadde wered a wolyper
And with the staf sche drow ay ner and ner
And wende an hit þes aleyn at þe fulle
And smot þe mellere on þe pylede sculle
And doun he goth harow I deye
These clerkys bete hym wel and lete hym lye
And hastede hem and toke here leue anon
And ek here mele and on here woye þey gon
And at þe melle ȝit þey toke here kake
Of half a buschel flour wol wel Ibake


Thus is þe proude mellere wel Ibete
And hath Ilost the gryndyng of þe wete
And payed for þe souper euery del  
Of aleyn and of Iohn þat bete hym wel
Hese wyf is swyuyd and hese doughtyr als
Lo swich It is a mellere to ben fals
And þerfore this prouerbe is seyd ful soth
Hym thar not wene wel þat euele doth
A gylour schal hym self begylede be
And god þat settyth hye in mageste
Save all þese cumpanyis grate and smale
Thus haue I quit þe mellere in myn tale
THe cook of lundene whil þe reue spak
ffor ioye hym thouȝte he clawede hym on þe bak
Ha ha ha for cristys passyoun
This mellere hadde a scharp conclusyoun
Vp on his argument of herbergage
Wel seyde salamon  on his langage
Ne brynge not euery with in to þyn hous
ffor herberwynge be nyȝte is perlyous
Wel auȝte a man avysede for to be
Whom þat he brouȝte in to hese priuyte
I preye to god so ȝeue me sorwe and care
Syn euere I highte hoge of ware
Herde I euere a mellere betere Iset a werke
He hadde a Iape of maleys in þe derke
But god forbede þat we stentyn here
And þerfore ȝif ȝe wouche saf to here
A tale of me þat am a pore man
I wele ȝow telle as wel as euere I can
A lytyl Iape what fel in oure cete
Oure ost answerde and seyde I graunte it þe
Now telle on roger and loke þat it be good
ffor manye a paste hast þou letyn blod
And manye a rakke of douere hast þou sold
That hath ben twyes hot and twyes cold  
Of manye a pilgrym hast þou cristis curs
ffor of thyn persele ȝit thy fare þe wers
That þey han etyn with thyn stobil goos
ffor in thyn schoppe is manye a flye los
Now telle on gentyl roger be þyn name
But ȝit I preye þe be not wroth for game
A man may sey ful soth in game and play
Thow seyst ful soth quod roger be myn fay


But sooth pley quaad pley as þe flemyng seyth
And þerfore herry bayly be þyn feyth
Be þou not wroth er we partyn here
Thow þat myn tale be of an ostelere
But natheles I wele nat telle it ȝet
But er we parte Iwis þou schat be quit
And þerwithal he low and made chere
And seyde hese tale as ȝe schal aftyr here
A Prentis whilom dwellid in oure citee  
And of a craft of vitalers was he
Gaillard he was as golfynche in þe schawe
Broun as bery a proper short felawe
With lokkes blake Ikempt ful fetisly
Daunce he kouþe so wel and Iolyly
That he clepid perkyn reueilloure
He was as ful of loue and paramour
As is þe hive ful of hony swete
Wel was þe wenche with him myght mete
At euery bridale wold he synge and hoppe
He louede bette þe tauerne þan þe shoppe
ffor whan þer any ridynge was in chepe  
Out of þe Shoppe þeder wold he lepe
Til þat he had al þe sight Iseyn
And daunced wel wold he not come agayne
And gedrid hym mony of his sort
To hoppe and synge and make suche disport
And þere þey setten steuene for to mete
To pleyn at þe dys in suche a strete
ffor in þe toun nas ner no prentis
That fairer couþe cast a peyre of dys
Then perkyn couth and þerto he was free
Of his dispence in place of pryuyte
That fonde his maister wel in his chaffare
ffor ofte tyme he fonde his box ful bare
ffor sikirly a prentis reuelour
    
His maystir shuld it in his shep abye
Al haue not part of þe mynstralcie
ffor theft and riot þei ben conuertible
Al can he pleye on geterne or rubible


Reuel and trouth as in lowe degree
They ben ful wroth al day as men may see
This Iolye prentis with his mayster boode
Til he were nyghe oute of his prentishoode
Al were he snybbit erly and late
And somtyme lad with Reuel to Newgate
But at last his maystir him byþoght
Vpon a day whan he his paper sought
Of a prouerbe þat saith þis same word
Wel bet is roten appel oute of hoorde
Than þat it rotet alle þe remenant
So farith it by a ryocous seruant
It is ful lasse harme to late hym passe
Than he shend alle þe seruauntz in þe place
Therfore his maystir ȝaf him a quytaunce
And bade him go with sorow and myschaunce
And þus this Ioly prentis had his leuee  
Now let hym Riot al þe nyght or leue
And for ther is no theof withoute a loke
That helpith hym to wasten and to sowke
Of þat he bribe can or borow may
Anoon he sent his bede and his array
Vn to a couper of his owne soort
That loued dys Reuel and disport
And had a wif þat held for contynaunce
A shope and swyfed for hir sustynaunce
oure Oste saugh well that the bright sonne
The arke of his artaficiall day had ronne
The fourthe parte and half an houre and more
And though he were not deep experte in lore
He wist it was the xviij day
Of Aprill that is messager to May
And saugh well that the schadow of euery tre
Was as in lengthe the same quantite
That was the body erecte that causid it
And þerfore by þe schadewe he tok hese wit  
That phebus which þat schon so cler and bryȝt
Degreis fyue and forty Iclombe on hyȝt
And for þat day as in þat latytude
It was ten of þe clok he gan conclude
And sodeynly he plyȝte hese hors aboute
Lordyngis quod he I warne ȝow al þis route
The fourte party of þis day is gon
Now for þe loue of god and seynt Iohn
Leseth no tyme as fer forth as ȝe may
Lordyngis it wastyth nyȝt and day
And stelyth from vs what priuyly slepynge
And what þerwith neclygence In oure wakynge
As doth þe strem þat turnyth neuere ageyn
Dessendynge from þe monteyn Into pleyn
Wel can senykeke and manye a phylisofere
Bewaylyn tyme more þan gold in cofere
ffor los of catel may recouerede be
But los of tyme schendyth vs quod he


It wele not come ageyn withoutyn drede
No more þan wele malkenys maydynhede
Whan sche hath lost it in here wantounnesse
Let vs not moulyn þus in ydylnesse
Syre man of lawe so haue ȝe blys
Telle vs a tale now as forward is
Ȝe ben submyttit þour ȝoure fre assent
To stondyn in þis cas at myn Iugement
Aquytht ȝow now of ȝoure beheste
Þanne haue ȝe don ȝoure deuyr at þe leste
Host quod he depardeux I assente
To brekyn forward is not myn entente
Byheste is dette and I wele holde fayn
Al myn beheste I can no betere seyn
ffor swich lawe as man ȝeuyth anoþer wyȝt
He schulde hym selue vse it be right
Thus wele oure tyxt  but natheles serteyn
I can not now non thrifty tale seyn  
That Chaucer thoughte he can but lewedely
On metris and on rymyng craftyly
As seyde hem in swich engelych as he can
Of olde tyme as knowyth manye a man
And ȝif he haue not seyde hem leue broþer
In on bok he hath seyd hem in a noþer
ffor he hath told of louerys vp and down
Mo þan ouyde made of mencyoun 
In hese epistell þat ben ful olde
What schulde I telle hem syn þat þey ben tolde
In ȝouthe he made of Ceys and alceoun
And syþe haþ he spoke of euerychon
These nobele wyuys and þese loueris ek
Who so þat wole hese large volum sek
Clepid þe seyntis legende of cupide
There may he se þe large woundis wyde
Of lucresse and of babiloyn Tisbee
The swerd of dido for þe false Enee


The tre of phill for here demephoun
The pleynt of dyane and of hermyoun
Of adryane and of Isiphilee
The barayne yle standynge in þe se
The dreynte leandere for hese erro
The terys of elyne and ek þe wo
Of brixseyde and of þe ladomya
The cruelte of þe quene media
Thy lityl childeryn hangynge by þe hals
ffor thy Iason þat was in loue so fals
O ypermystre penolopee Alceste
Ȝoure wifhod be commendit with þe beste
But serteynly no word wrytyh he
Of thilk ensaumple of Canacee
That louede here owene broþer synfully
Of swiche cursede storyis I seye fy
Or ellis of Thiro appolonyus

Byrafte hys douȝtir hir Maydenhede
þat ys so horrible a tale for to here
Whan he hir þrowe þorough þe pament
And þfore he of full avisement
Wolde nevere write in none of his sermones
Of whiche vnkynde abhomynacions
Ne I· ne wil non reherse if þat I may
But of my tale how shalle doo þis day
Me were lothe he lykned douteles
To Muses þat men clepen pieriedes
Methamorphaseos wot wat y mene
But natheles I ne reche not a bene
Thoughe ·y· come after hym with aw bake
I speke in prose and let hym Rymes make
And with þat worde he with a sobre chere
Bygan his tale as ye shul after here
Ohatfulle harme condicion of pouert
With thrust with colde with hungre so confunded
To asken helpe þe shameth in þine hert
If þou now axe with nede arte þou so wounded
That verray nede vnwrappid al þi wounde hyd  
Maugre þine hede þou moste for Indegens
Or stele or begge or borowe þi dispense
Thou blamest crist and seyst fulle vtterly
He in his departith rychesse temporal
Thy neghboure þou witest synfully
And seyste þou haste to lytelle and he hath alle
Par fay seyste þou some tyme þou reken shalle
Whan þat his tayle shal brenne in þe glede
ffor he nouȝt helpith nedefulle in her nede
Herkene what ys þe menynge of þe wise
Bet is to dien þan to haue Indigence ·
Thy self neghbore wol þe dispice
If þou be pore fare wele þi reuerence
Ȝet of þe wise man take þis sentence ·
Alle dayes of pore men be wykke
Be ware þerfore or þou com in þat prik 
If þou be pore þi Brother hatith þe
Alle þi ffrendes fleen fro þe Allas ·
O riche merchantes ful of wele be ȝe
O noble prudent folke as in þis cas
youre bagges buth not fullyd with ambes ais
But with sys synke þat renneth of your chaunce
At cristes masse merie may ye daunce


Ȝe sechen londe and See for your wynnynges
As wyse folkes þat knowen alle þe staat 
Of regnes ye ben fadres and tydynges
And tales bothen of pees and debate
I were riȝt nowe of talys dissolate
Nere þat a marchaunt goon ys many ·a· yeere
Me taught a tale whiche as · ȝe shal here
This senatourys wif hyre aunte was
But for al þat sche knew hyre neuere þe more
I wele no lengere taryen in þis cas
But to kyng alla which I spak of ȝore
That for his wyf wepith and sykyth sore
I wele returne and lete I wele custaunce
Vndyr þe senatourys gouernaunce
In Surry whilom dwellede a cmpaignye  
Of chapmen riche and þerto sadde and trewe
That wide where sentyn here spicerye
Clothis of gold and satynys ryche of hewe
Here chaffare was so thrifty and so newe
That euery wight hath deynte to chaffare
With hem and ek to sellen hem here ware
Now fil it that þe maysteris of þat sort
Han shapyn hem to rome for to wende
Were it for chapmanhod or for disport
Non oþer message wolde he dedyr sende
But comyn hem self to rome þis is thende
And in swich place as thoghte hem thawauntage
ffor hire entent þey take hire herbergage
Soiournyd han þese marchauntis in þat toun
A serteyn tyme as fel to here plesaunce
But so befel þat thexselent renoun
Of themperourys doghter dame Custaunce
Reportid was with euery circumstance
Vnto thys surryne marchantys in swich wise
ffrom day to day as I schal ȝow deuyse
This was the comune voys of euery man
Oure emperoure of rome god hym se
A doughtir hath þat syn þe world began
To rekene as wel here goodnes as here beute
Was neuere swich anoþer as is sche
I preye to god in honour here sustene
And wolde sche were of al Europe þe quene


In here is high beute withoute pryde
Ȝouthe withoute grenehede or folye
To alle here werkys vertu is here gyde
Humblesse hath slayn in here al tyrannye
Sche is myrour of alle curteysye
Here herte is verray chambyr of holynesse
Hire hand mynystre of fredom for almesse
And al þis voys was soth as god is trewe  
But now to purpos lat vs turne ageyn
These marchantys han don frauȝt here schepis newe
And whan þey han þis blysful maydyn seyn
Hom to surry ben þey went ful feyn
And on here nedys as þey don ful ȝore 
And lyuen in wele I can sey ȝow no more
Now fil it þat these marchantys stode in grace
Of hym þat was þe soudon of surrye
ffor whan þey come from ony strange place
He wolde of hese benygne curteysye
Make hem good cher and besyly espye
Tydyngis of sundery regnys for to lere
The wonderis þat he myghte sen or here
Amongis oþere thyngis specially
These marchauntis han hym told of dame Custaunce
So gret noblesse in ernest certeynly
That this soudan hath cauȝt so gret plesaunce
To han hyre fygure in hese remembraunce
And al hese lust and al hese besy cure
Was for to loue here whil his lyf may dure
Perauenture in thilke large boke
Which þat clepid is þe heuene Iwretyn was
With sterrys whan þat he hese berthe tok
That he for loue schulde han hese deth allas


ffor in þe sterris clerere than is glas
Is wrete god wot ho so coude it rede
The deth of euery man  with outyn any drede
In sterrys manye a wyntyr there beforn
Was wretyn þe deth of ector achilles
Of pompeye Ielyus er þey were born
The stryf of thebes and of hercules
Of sampson Thurnus and of socrates
The deth but menys wittys ben so dulle
That no with can wel rede it at þe fulle
This soudon for hese priuy conseyl sente  
And schortely of þis matiere for to pace
He hath to hem declarede his entente
And seyde serteyn but he myȝte han grace
To han custaunce withinne a lytyl space
He nas but ded and chargede hem in hye
To schapyn for hese lyf sum remedye
Dyuerse men dyuerse thyngys seydyn
They argumentyn and castyn vp and doun
Manye a subtyle resoun forth þey leydyn
They spekyn of Magyk and Abusioūn
But fynally as in conclusioun
They can not sen in that non auantage
Ne in non othir woye saue maryage
Thanne sawe they þerin swich difficulte
Be weye of resoun for to speke al pleeyn
Be cause þere was  swich dyuercyte
Betwethyn here bothe lawys þat þey seyn
They trowede that no crystene prynce wolde fayn
Weddyn his chyld vndyr oure lawys swete
That vs was tauȝt be mahoun oure prophete


And he answerde raþere than I lese
Constance I wele ben cristened douteles
I mote ben hers  I may non oþer chese
I prey ȝow holde ȝoure argument in pes
Sauyth myn lyf and beth nat recheles
To getyn here that hath myn lyf in cure
ffor in þis wo I may not longe endure
What nedyth grettere dilatacioun
I sey be tretys and enbassadrye
And bi þe popis mediacioun
And al the cherch and þe chyualrye
That in distruccioun of mametrye
And in encres of Crystes lawe dere
They ben ecordit so as ȝe schal here
How þat the soudan and hese baronage  
And alle hese lyges schulde cristenede be
And he schal haue custaunce in maryage
And serteyn gold I not what quantyte
And heer to fyndyn sufficient suretee
This same acord was sworn on eyþer syde
Now fayre Custaunce almyȝty god ȝow gyde
Now wolde sum men waytyn as I gesse
Ȝit I schulde telle al þe puruyaunce
That þe emperour of his greete noblesse
Hath schapyn for hese doughtur dame Custaunce
Wel may men knowe þat so gret ordenaunce
May no man telle in swich a lytyl clause
As was arayed for so high a cause
Byschopis ben schapyn with here for to wende
Lordyngis ladyis knyȝtis of renoun
And oþere folk Inowe this is the ende
And notyfyed is thorw out þe toun


That euery knyȝt with gret deuocioun
Schulde preye crist þat he this maryage
Receyue In gre and spede þis viage
The day is come of here departynge
I sey the woful fatal day is come
That þere may be no lengere taryinge
But forward þey hem drese alle and some
Custaunce that was with sorwe al ouyrcome
fful pale aryst and dreseth here to wende
ffor weel sche seeth there is non oþer ende
Allas no wondir is it þow sche wepte
That schal be sent into straunge nacioun
ffor frendys that so tenderely here kepte
And to ben boundyn vndyr subieccyoun
Of on sche knowyth not hese condicioun
Housbondis ben alle goode and han been ȝore
That knowyn wyuys I dar sey ȝow no moore
ffadyr sche seyde þyn wrechede chyld Custaunce  
Thi ȝonge douȝty fosterede vp so softe
And ȝe myn modyr myn souereyn plesaunce
Ouer alle thynge out take cryst on lofte
Custaunce ȝore child hire recomaundyth ofte
Vnto ȝoure grace for I schal to surrye
Ne schal I neuere sen ȝow more with eye
Allas vnto þe barbre nacioun
I muste anon sithe þat it is ȝoure wille
But cryst þat starf for our redempcyoun
So ȝeue me grace hese hestis to fulfylle
I wreche woman no fors thow I spille
Wemen are bore to thraldam and penaunce
And to ben vndyr manys gouernaunce


I trowe at troye whan pirrus brak þe wal
Or ylion brende at thebes the cetee
Nat rome for þe harm þorw hanybal
That romaynys han enqueschid tymys three
Nas herd swich tendere wepyng for pete
As in the chaumbere was for here departynge
But forth sche muste  where so sche wepe or synge
O fyrste moeuyng crewel fyrmament
With thi dyurnal which þat croudist ay
And hurlyst al from est til occident
That naturally wolde holde anoþer way
Thi croudyng set þe heuene in swich aray
At þe begynynge of this ferse viage
That crewel mars hath slaye þis maryage
Infortunat ascendent tortuous
Of which þe lord is helpeles falle allas
Out of hese angels into þe derkeste hous
O mars o ataȝer as in this cas
O febele mone vnhappi ben thi pas
Thow knyttist þe þere þat art not reseyuyd
There þow were wel from thens art thow weyuyd
Inprudent Emperour of Rome allas  
Whas þere no philisophere in al thyn toun
Is no tyme bet þan oþer in swich cas
Of viage is þere non eleccioun
And namely to folk of high condicioun
Nat whan a rote is of a burthe Iknowe
Allas we ben to lewede and to slowe
To schip is brouȝt this woful fayre mayde
Solempnely with euery circumstaunce
Now Ihesu crist be with ȝow alle sche seide
There is namore but fare wel fayre Custaunce


Sche peynyth here to make good cuntenaunce
And forth I lete here sayle in this manere
And turne I wele ageyn to myn matere
The modyr of the soudon welle of vices
Espyed hath here sonys pleyn entente
How he wolde lete his olde sacrifises
And ryȝt anon sche for here conseyl sente
And they be come to knowe what sche mente
And whan assembelede were þe folk en feere
Sche sette here doun and seyde as ȝe schal here
Lordys quod sche ȝe heryn euerychon
How þat myn sone in poynt is for to lete
The holy lawis of oure alkaron
Ȝeuen be goddys message Makomete
But on a wow to grete god I heete
The lyf schal raþere out of myn body sterte
On makometes lawe out of myn herte
What schulde vs tydyn of this newe lawe
But thraldam to oure bodyis and penaunce
And aftyr in helle for to be drawe
ffor we reneyede mahoun oure creaunce
But lordis wele ȝe makyn a suraunce
As I schal seyn assentynge to myn lore
And I schal make vs saf for euere more
They sworyn and assentyn euery man  
To lyue with hyre and deye and by here stonde
And eueryche in þe beste wyse sche can
To strenthe here schal alle here frendis fonde
And sche hath this empryse take on honde
Whiche ȝe schal here that I schal deuyse
An to hem alle sche spak ryth in þis wyse


We schul fyrst feyne vs cristenedam to take
Cold watyr schal nat greue vs but a lite
And I schal swich a feste and reuel make
That as I trowe I schal the soudon quyte
ffor thow hese wyf be crystenede neuere so whyte
Sche schal han neede to wasche awey the reede
Thow sche a funt ful of watyr with here leede
O soudonesse roote of iniquite
Virago thow semiame the secunde
O serpent vndyr femynynyte
Lyk to the serpent deepe in helle Ibounde
O feynede woman al that may conffounde
Vertu and innocence thour thyn maleyce
Is bred in þe  as nest in euery vice
O satan enuyous syn thilke day
That þou were chasede þour oure erytage
Wel knowyst þou to wemen þe elde way
Thow madist eua brynge vs in seruage
Thow wilt fordon this cristene maryage
Thyn Instreument so weyleawey the whyle
Makyst þou of wemen wan þou wit begile
This soudonesse whom I þus blame and warye
Let pryuyly hire conseyl gon here way
What schulde I in this tale lengere tarye
Sche rydith to þe soudan on a day
And seyde he wolde receyue hire lay
And cristendom of prestis hondis fonge
Repentynge hire sche hethene was so longe
Besekynge hem to don here þat honour  
That sche muste haue þe crystene folk to feste
To plesyn hem I wele don myn labour
The soudon seyth I wele don at ȝoure heste


And kenelynge thankyth here of þat requeste
So glad he was he nyste what to seye
Sche kyste here sone  and hom sche goth here weye
Aryuede ben these crystene men to londe
In surrey with a gret solempne route
And hastiliche þis soudan sente hese sonde
ffyrst to hese modir and al hese regne aboute
And seyde hese wyf was comyn out of doute
And preyede hire to ryde aȝen þe quene
The honour of hese regne to sustene
Gret was þe pres and riche was tharay
Of surreynys and romeynys met in fere
The modyr of the soudan ryche and gay
Receyuyth hire with also glad a chere
As any modir myȝte hire douȝtyr dere
And to þe nexte sete þere be syde
A softe pas solempnely þey ryde
Noght trowe I þe triumphe of Iulius
Of which þat lucan makyth swich a bost
Was royallere ne more curyous
þan was thasemble of þis blysful ost
But þis scorpioun þis wekede gost
The soudonesse for al hyre flaterynge
Caste vndyr this ful mortali to stynge
The soudan comyth hym self sone aftyr this
So royali þat wondir is to telle
He wolcomyth hire with al ioye and blys
And þus in merthe and ioye I lete hem dwelle


The freut of this matiere is þat I telle
Whan tyme cam men thouȝte it for þe beste
That reuel stynte and men gone to here reste
The tyme cam this olde soudonesse  
Ordeynyd hath this feste of which I telle
And to þe feste cristene folk hym dresse
In general ȝe bothe ȝynge and olde
Here may men feste and rialte beholde
And deynteis mo þan I can ȝow deuyse
But al to dere they bouȝte it er they ryse
O sodeyn wo that euere art successour
To wordely blysse spreynt with bittyrnesse
Thende of the ioye of oure wordely labour
Who occupiet the fyn of oure gladnesse
Herkene þis conseyl for thyn sekyrnesse
Vpon thyn glade day haue in thyn mynde
The onwar wo or harm that comyth behynde
ffor schortely for to tellyn at on word
The soudon and the crystene euerychone
Ben al tohewe and stikid at the bord
But it were only dame custaunce alone
This olde soudanesse cursede crone
Hath with here frendis don this curssede dede
ffor sche here selue wolde at the cuntre lede
Ne þere was surreyn non that was conuertid
That of the conseyl of the soudon wot
That he was hewe er that he asterted
And custaunce han they take anon fot hot
And in a schip al stereles god wot
They han hire set and bidde hire lerne sayle
Out of surrie ageyn ward to ytayle


A serteyn trosor that sche theþer ladde
And soth to sayn vitayle gret plente
They han hyre ȝeuyn and clothis ech sche hadde
And forth sche saylyth in the salte see
O myn custaunce ful of benyngnete
O emperouris douȝtyr ȝonge dere
He that is lord of fortune be thi stere
Sche blysseth hire and with ful pitous voys  
On to the Croys of crist thus seyde sche
O cler o wilful auter holy cros
Reed of the lambis blod ful of pite
That wesch þe world from old iniquite
Me from the fend and from hese clawis kepe
That day þat I schal drenchyn in þe deepe
Victorious tre protexioun of trewe
That only worthy were for to bere
The kyng of heuene withese woundis newe
The white lomb that hurt was wyt a spere
fflemere of feendis out of hym and hire
On which thyn lyfis feythfully extenden
Me kep and ȝif me myȝt myn lyf to amenden
Ȝeerys and dayis fleth this creature
Torwout the strem of grece into strayte
Of marrok whiche that was hese auenture
On manye a sory Mel now may ȝe beyte
Aftyr hire deth ful ofte may sche wayte
Er than þe wylde wawys wole here dryue
Vnto the place there sche schal aryue
Men myȝtyn axsyn whi sche was not slayn
Ek at the feste ho myȝte hire body saue
And I answere to that demaunde agayn
Ho sauede daniel in þe orybele caue


There euery with saue he maystyr and knave
Was with the lyoun frete er he asterte
Non wigh but god þat he bar in hese herte
God lyste to schewe his wondyrful merakele
In hire for we schud sen hise myȝty werkys
Cryst which þat is  to euery harm tryakele
Be serteyn mene oftyn as knowyn klerkes
Doth thyng to serteyn ende þat ful derk is
To mannys wit that for oure ignoraunce
Ne kunne not knowe hese prudent puruyaunce
Now sythe sche was not at the feste slawee  
Who kepte hyre from the drenchynge in þe see
Who kepte Ionas in the fyschis mawee
Thil he was spoutid out at niniuee
Wel may men knowe it was no wiȝt but he
That kepte þe peple Ebrayk from here drenchynge
With dreye feet thorwout þe se passynge
Who bad the foure spirytis of tempest
That power han tanoyen lond and se
Bothe north and south and also west and est
Anoyeth neyþer se lond ne tree
Sothly the comaundour was hee
That from the tempest ay this woman kepte
As wel whan sche wok as whan sche slepte
Where myȝte this woman mete or drynk haue
Thre ȝer and more how lastyth hire vitayle
Ho fedde þe egipcien marye in þe caue
Or in desert no wiȝt but crist sauns fayle
ffyue thousent folk it was a gret meruayle
With louys fyue and fyschis too to feede
God sente hese foysoun at here moste neede


Sche dryuyth forth into oure occian
Thourout oure wilde see til at þe laste
Vndyr an hold þat nemenyn I ne can
ffor in northumbyrlond the wawis hire caste
And in þe se hire schip stekede so faste
That þens ne wolde it not of al a tide
The wyl of here was þat sche schulde abyde
The constabele of þe Castel doun is fare
To sen þis wrak and al þe schip he souȝte
And fond þis wery woman ful of care
He fond also þe tresore þat sche brouȝte
In hyre langage mercy sche besouȝte
The lyf out of hire body to twynne
Hire to delyuere of woo þat sche was inne
A maner latyn corupt was hire speche  
But algatis þerbi was sche vndirstonde
The Constabele whan hym lyste no lengere seche
This woful woman brouȝte he to the londe
Sche knelyth doun and thankyth godis sonde
But what sche was sche durste no man seye
ffor foul ne fayr thow þat sche schulde deye
Sche seyde sche was so masede in the see
That sche forgat hire mynde by hyre trouthe
The cunstabele hath of hire gret pite
And ek his wif that þey wepe for routhe
Sche was so diligent withoutyn slouthe
To serue and plese eueryche in þat place
That alle hyre louyn þat lokyn in hyre face
This constabil and dame hermengylt his wyf
Were payenys in þat cuntrey euery where
But Ermengylt louede hire ryȝt as hire lyf
And Custaunce hath so longe soiurnede þere


In orisounys with manye a bittere tere
Til Ihesu hath conuertede þour hese grace
Dame Ermengilt Constabellesse of þat place
In al þat lond no cristene durste at route
Alle cristen folk ben fled from þat cuntre
Thour poynyms þat conqueredyn al aboute
The plagis of the north and se
To walis fledde þe cristianyte
Of olde brytunys dwellynge in þis yle
There was hire refeut for the mene while
But ȝit nere cristene britounys so exiled
þat þere nere some þat in hire priuite
Honourede crist and hethene folk begilede
And ngh þe castel swich þere dweltyn thre
That on of hem was blynd and myȝte not se
But it were with þe ilke eyen of hise mynde
Wit whiche men sen aftyr þat þey ben blynde
Bryȝt was þe sune as in þat someris day  
ffor which þe Constabel and hese wyf also
And custaunce hath Itake þe ryȝte way
Toward þe se a furlong wey or to
To pleyen and to romyn too and fro
And in hire walk þis blynde man þey mette
Crokid and old with eyen faste Ischette
In name of cryst cryede þis blynde Erytoun
Dame Hermengelt ȝif me myn syȝt ageyn
This lady wex afreyed of þe soun
Lest þat hire husbonde schortly for  seyn
Wolde hire for ihesu crist han slayn
Til Custaunce made hire bold and bad hire for to werche
The wil of crist as doughtyr of hise cherche


The Constabele wex abaschid of that syȝt
And seyde what amountyh al þis fare
Custaunce answere syre it is cristis myȝt
That helpith folk out of þe fendis snare
And so fer forth sche gan oure lay declare
That sche þe Constabele er þan it was eue
Conuertid and on cryst made hym bileue
This Constabele was no þyng lord of þis place
Of whiche I speke þere he constaunce fond
But kepte it strongely manye a wynteris space
Vndir alla kyng of al northhumbir londe
That was ful wys and worthi of hese honde
Ageyn þe skottis as men may wel here
But turne I wele agen to myn matyere
Satan þat euere wayth vs to begyle
Saugh of Custaunce al þe perfeccioun
And caste anon how he myȝte quite hire while
And made a ȝong knght þat dwellede in þat toun
Loue hire so hote of foul affeccioun
That verayly hym thouȝte he schulde spille
But he of hire myȝte onys haue hese wille
He wowyth hire but it auaylyth nouȝt  
Sche wolde don no synne be no weye
And for dispit he compassith in his thouȝt
To makyn hyre on schamful deth to deye
He waythith whan þe Constable is aweye
And priui vpon a nyȝt he crepte
Into Hermengildis chaumbere whil sche slepte
Wery forwakede in hire orysouns
Slepith custaunce and hemegild also
This knyȝt þour satanys temptacions
Al softeli is to þe bed Igo


And kitte þe throte of Hermegild a too
And leyde þe blodi knyf be dame Custaunce
And wente his wey þere god ȝyf hym myschaunce
Sone aftyr comyth this Constabele hom ageyn
And ek Alla þat kyng was of þat lond 
And saw his wif dispitously Islayn
ffor which ful ofte he wepte and wrong here hon
And in þe bed þe blody knyf he fond
By dame Constance Allas what myȝte sche seye
ffor werray woo hire wit was al aweye
To kyng alla was told þis tale Mischaunce
And ek þe tyme where and in what wyse
That in a schyp was founde þis custaunce
As here beforn þat ȝe han herd deuyse
The kyngis herte of pete gan to gryse
Whan he saw so benygne a creature
ffalle in desese and in mysauenture
ffor as þe lomb toward þe deth is brouȝt
So stant this innocent byfore þe kynge
This false knyȝt that hath this tresoun wrought
Beryth hire on honde þat sche hath don þis thynge
But natheles þere was gret mornyng
Among the puple and seyn þey can not gesse
That sche hadde don so gret a wekedenesse
ffor they han seyn hire so vertuous  
And louynge hermengild ryȝt as hire lyf
Of þis bar witnesse eueryche in that hous
Saue he þat hermengelt slow with his knyf
This gentil kyng hath cauȝt a gret motyf
Of this witnesse and thoght he wolde enquire
Deppere in this trouthe for to lere


Allas Custaunce þou hast no chaumpioun
Ne fyȝte canst þou so weyleawey
But he that starf for oure redempcioun
And bond satan and ȝit lyth þere he lay
So be þeyn stronge champioun þis day
ffor but ȝif cryst opyn merakele kythe
Withoutyn gilt þou schat ben slayn aswythe
Sche sette hire doun on kneis and thus sche seyde
Inmortal god þat sauedist susanne
ffrom false blame and þou merciful mayde
Marye I mene douȝtyr to seynt ann
Byforn hos child aungell synge osanne
If I be gilteles of this felonye
Myn socour be for ellis schal I deye
Han ȝe nat seyn sumtyme a pale face
Among a pres of hym þat hath be lad
Toward hese deth where as he gat no grace
And swich a colour in hese face hath had
Men myȝte knowe hise face þat was bestad
Amongis alle þe facis in þat route
So stant custaunce and lokyth hire a boute
O queenys lyuynge in prosperite
Duchesses and ȝe ladijs euerychone
Hauyth sum routhe of hire aduercite
An emperouris douȝtyr stant alone
Sche hath no wyȝt to whom to make hire mone
O blood royal þat standyst in þis drede
ffer ben thyne frendis at thi grete nede
This alla kyng hath swich compascioun  
As gentyl herte is ful fyld of pite
That from hyse eyen ran the watyr doun
Now hastyfliche do feche a bok quod he


And ȝif this knȝt wele swere þat sche
This woman slow ȝit wele we vs auyse
Hom þat we wele þat schal ben oure Iustyse
A brytoun bok wrytyn with euaungilis
Was fet in on this bok he swor anon
Sche gilty was and in the mene whilis
An hand hym smot vpon the nekke bon
That doun he fyl atonys as a ston
And bothe hise eyen broste vp on hise face
In syȝte of euery body in þat place
A woys was herd in general audience
And seyde þou hast disclaunderede gilteles
The douȝtyr of holy cherche in high presence
Thus hast þou don and ȝit I holde myn pees
Of this mervayle agast was al þe pres
As masede folk they stodyn euerychone
ffor drede of wreche saue Custaunce allone
Gret was þe dred and ek þe repentaunce
Of hem þat han wrong suspecioun
Vpon þis sely Innocent custaunce
And for this myrakele in conclusioun
And by Custauncis mediacioun
The kyng and manye a noþer in þat place
Conuertede were thankid be godis grace
This false knyȝt was slayn for hise ontrouthe
Be Iugement of alla hastifly
And ȝit Custaustaunce hadde of hise deth routhe
And aftyr this Ihesus of hise mercy
Made alla weddyn solempnely
This holy maydyn þat is so bryȝt and scheene
And þus hath Cryst mad Custaunce a queene


But who was woful ȝif I scal not lye  
Of this weddyng but donegild and no mo
The kyngis modir ful of tyrannye
Hire thouȝt hire curssede herte brast a to
Sche wolde not hire sone hadde don so
Hire thouȝte a dispit þat he schulde take
So straunge a creature vnto hise make
Me lyste not of þe chaf nor of þe stre
Makyn so long a tale as of þe corn
What sholde I telle of the royalte
At mariage or wich cours goth beforn
Who blowith in a trompe or in an horn
The freut of eueri tale is for to seye
They ete and drynke and daunce and synge and pleye
Thei gon to bedde as it was skele and ryȝt
ffor þow þat wiuys ben ful holye thyngis
They muste takyn in pacience at nyȝt
Swiche manere of necessarijs as ben plesyngis
To folk þat han wedit hem with ryngis
And leyn a lityl here holynesse asyde
As for þe tyme it may non oþer betyde
On hire he gat a knave child anon
And to a bischop and his constabele ek
He tok hise wyf to kepe whan he is gon
To skotlondeward hise fomen for to seke
Now fayre custaunce þat is so vmble and meke
So longe is gon with childe til þat stille
Sche halt hire chaumbere abydynge cristis wille
The tyme is come a knaue child sche beere
Mauricyus at þe funtston þey hym calle
This Constabele doth forth a massanger
And wrot onto his kyng þat clepid was alle


How þat this blisful tydyng is byfalle
And oþere tydyngis spedful for to seye
He taath þe lettere and forth he goth hise weye
This massanger to don his auauntage  
Vnto þe kyngis modyr ridyth swythe
And saluyth hire ful fare in hyre langage
Madame quod he ȝe may ben glad and blyþe
And thankede god a hunderede thousent sythe
Myn lady quen hath child withoutyn doute
To Ioye and blysse to al þe regne aboute
Lo here þe letteris selede of þis thyng
That I mot bere with þe haste I may
Ȝif ȝe wele ouȝt onto ȝoure sone þe kyng
I am ȝoure seruaunt bothe nyȝt and day
Donegild answerede as now at þis tyme nay
But here al nyght I wele þou take þyn reste
To morwe wele I seye þe what me leste
This massangere drank faste ale and wyn
And stole were hise letteris priuyly
Out of his box whil he slepte as a swyn
And countyrfetid was ful subtilly
Anoþer lettere wrouȝt ful synfully
Vnto þe kyng direckt of this matere
ffrom his Constabil as ȝe schal aftyr here
The lettere spak þe quen delyuerede was
Of so orible and fendlyche cryature
That in þe castel non so hardy was
That ony while durste þere endure
The modyr was an elf be nature
Icomyn by charmys or bi socerye
And euery wyȝt hath hire cumpanye


Wo was this kyng whan he þis lettere hath seyn
But to no wyȝt he tolde hise sorwis sore
But of hyse owene hand he wrot ageyn
Wolcome þe sonde of cryst for euere more
To me that am now lernede in þis lore
Lord wolcome be thyn lust and þyn plesaunce
Myn lust I putte al in thyn ordenaunce
Kepith this child al be it foul or fayr  
And ek myn wyf onto myn hom comynge
Cryst whan hym lyste may sende me an eyr
More agriable þan this to myn lykynge
This lettere he selyth pryuyly wepynge
Whiche to þe massangere was take sone
And forth he goth þere is no more to done
O Massanger fulfild of dronkenesse
Strong is thi breth thi lemys falteryn ay
And þou bewreyest alle sekerenesse
Thyn mynde is lorn þou iangelist as a Iay
Thyn face is turnede in a newe aray
There dronkenesse regnyth in ony route
There is no conseyl hid withoutyn doute
O donegilt I haue non engelissh dygne
Vnto þyn maleys and thi tyrannye
And þerfore to þe fend I þe resigne
Let hym endyte of thyn tratorye
ffy mannyssh fy  o nay by god I lye
ffy fendelyche spirit for I dar wel telle
Thow þow here walke thyn spyrit is in helle
This Massanger comyth from þe kyng ageyn
And at þe kyngis moderis court he lyghte
And sche was of þe massenger ful fayn
And plesede hym in al þat euere sche myȝte


He drank and wel hise gerdyl vndyr pyȝt
He slepith and he snortith in hise gyse
Al nyȝt tyl þe sunne gan aryse
Eft were hise letterys stolyn euerychon
And counterfetid letterys in þis wyse
The kyng comaundyth hise constablis anon
Vp peyne of hangynge and heigh Iuyse
That he ne schulde suffere in no wyse
Custaunce in whith his regne for tabyde
Thre dayis and a quartyr of a tide
But in þe same schip as he hire fond  
Hire and hyr ȝenge sone and al hire geere
He schulde putte and croude from þe lond
And charge hire þat sche neuere eft come þere
O myn custaunce wel may þy gost haue fere
And slepynge in þyn drem han penaunce
Whan donegilt caste al þis ordenaunce
This messenger on morwe he wok
Onto þe castel holt þe neste wey
And to þe constabele he þe lettere tok
And whan þat he þis pitous lettere say
fful ofte he seyde allas and weyleaway
Lord crist how may þis world endure
So ful of synne is manye a cryature
O myȝti god ȝif þat it be þyn wille
Sith þou art ryȝtful Iuge how may þis be
That þou wit suffere innocentis to spille
And wekede folk regnyn in prosperite
O goode Custaunce allas so wo is me
þat I mote be þyn turmentour or deye
On schamys deth þere is non oþer weye


Wepyn bothe ȝynge and olde in þat place
Whan þat þe kyng his cursede letere sente
And Custaunce with a dedly pale face
The forte day toward hire schip sche wente
But natheles sche takyth in good entente
The wil of crist and knelynge on þe stronde
Sche seyde lord ay wolcome be þyn sonde
He þat me kepte from þe false blame
Whil I was on þe lond amongis ȝow
He can me kepe from harm and ek from schame
In þe salte se al þow I se nat how
As strong as euere he was he is now
In hym troste I and hyse modyr dere
That is to me myn sayl and ek myn stere
Hyre lytyl child lay wepynge in hire arm  
And knelynge pitously to hym sche seyde
Pes lityl sone I wele don þe non harm
With þat hire couerchif ouer hire hed sche bryde
And ouer hise lityl eyen sche it leyd
And in hyre arm sche lullede it ful faste
And into heuene hyre eyen vp sche caste
Modyr quod sche and mayde  bryȝte marye
Soth is þat þour wemanys eggement
Man kynde was lorn and dampnede for to deye
ffor wich þyn chyld was on a cros Iret
Thi blysful eyen saw al his turment
Thanne is þere non comparisoun betwene
Thi wo and any wo  man may sustene
Thow saw þyn child slawyn before þyn eyen
And ȝit now lyuyth my lityl child parfey
Now lady bryȝt to whom alle folk now cryen
Thow glorye of womanhede fayre may


Thow hauene of refut bryȝte sterre of day
Rewe on myn child þat of þyn gentillesse
Rewist on euery reuful in destresse
O lityl child allas what is þyn gilt
That neuere wroughtist synne as ȝit parde
Whi wolde thyn harde fadyr han þe spilt
O mercy dere constabele quod sche
As lat myn lytil child dwelle here with þe
And ȝif þou darst not sauyn hym from blame
So kysse hym onys in hese faderys name
Therwith sche lokith bakward to þe londe
And seyde farewe housbonde routheles
And vp sche rist and walkyth doun þe stronde
Toward þe schip here folwyth al þe pres
And euere sche preyeth hire child to holde hise pes
And takyth hire leue and with an holy entente
Sche blysseth hire and into schip sche wente
Vitaylid was þe schip it is no drede  
Habundaunt for hyre ful longe space
And oþere necessaryis þat schuldyn nede
Sche hadde Inow haryed be godis grace
ffor wynd and wedyr almyȝty god purchase
And brynge hire hom I can no betere seye
But in þe se sche dryuyth forth hire weye
Alla þe kyng comyth hom soone aftyr þis
Onto þe Castel whiche I tolde
And axsith where þat his wif and his child is
The Constabele gan aboute hise herte colde


And pleynly al þe manere hym tolde
As ȝe han herd I can telle it no bettre
As schewith þe kyng his sel and hise lettere
And seyde lord as ȝe comaundede me
Vp peyne of deth so haue I do serteyn
This massanger turmentid was tyl he
Moste beknowe and telle plat and pleyn
ffrom nyȝt to nyȝt what place he hadde leyn
And þus by wit and subtyl Inquyrynge
Ymagined was bi hom þis harm gan sprynge
The hand was knowe þat þe lettere wrot
And al þe venym of þis cursede dede
But in what wise serteynli I not
Theffect is þis þat Alla out of drede
His modyr slow þat may men pleynly rede
ffor þat sche traytour was to hire legiaunce
Thus endyth donegild with myschaunce
The sorwe þat þis alla nyȝt and day
Makith for his wif and hise child also
Ther is no tunge þat it telle may
But now wolde I onto Custaunce go
That fletyth in þe se in peyne and wo
ffyue ȝer and more as lykede cristis sonde
Er þat hir schip aprochede to þe londe
Vndyr an hethene castel at þe laste  
Of which þe name in myn tixt not I fynde
Custaunce and ek hire child þe se vp caste
Almyȝty god þat sawith al mankynde
Haue on custaunce and of hire child sum mynde
that is fallyn in hethene hand eft sone
In poynt to spylle as I schal telle ȝow sone


Doun from þe castel comyth þere manye a wyȝt
To gauryn on þis wyȝt and on custaunce
But schortly from þe castel on a nyȝt
The lordis styward god ȝeue hym myschaunce
A thef that hadde reneyed oure creaunce
Cam into þe schip alone and seyde he schulde
Hire leman be wheþer sche wolde or nolde
Wo was þe wrechede woman þo begon
Hire child cryed and sche cryede pitously
Blysful marye halp hyre ryȝt anon
ffor with hire strogelyng wel and myȝtyly
The thef fel ouyr bord al sodeynly
And in þe se he dreynte for veniaunce
And þus hath cryst onwemmede kept custaunce
O foule lust of luxurye lo thyn ende
Not only þat þou feyntist manys mynde
But verayly þou wilt hise body schende
Thende of þy werk or of þynne lustis blynde
Is compleynynge how manyon may men fynde
That not for werk but only þe entente
To don þis synne ben owthir slayn or schente
How may þis wayke woman han þis strenthe
Hire to defende aȝen þis Renegat
O golyas vnmesurabe of lenthe
How myȝte dauid make þe so maat
So ȝong and of armeure so desolat
How durste he loke vpon þyn dredful face
Wel may men sen it was but godis grace
Ho ȝaf Iudyth corage or hardynesse  
To slen hym Olofernus in hise tente
And to delyueryn out of wrechedenesse
The peple of god I sey for þis entente


But ryȝt as god spyrit of vigour sente
To hym and sauede hym from myschaunce
So sente vigour and myȝt to Custaunce
fforth goth the schip þourout þe narwe mouth
Of Iubaltare  and Cepte dryuynge ay
Sumtyme west and sumtyme north and south
And sumtyme est ful many a wery day
Til Cristis modyr blyssede be sche ay
Hath schapyn þour hire endeles goodnesse
To make an ende of al hire heuynesse
Now lat vs stynte of Custaunce but a trowe
And speke we of þe romayn Emperour
That out of surry hath bi letterys knowe
The slauthe of Cristene folk and dishonoure
Don to his douȝtyr by a fals traytoure
I mene þe wikkede cursede soudonesse
That at þe feste let sle boþe more and lesse
ffor which þis emperour hath sent anor
His senatour with royal ordenaunce
And oþere lordis god wot many on
On surryens to take veniaunce
They brenne and slen and brynge hem to myschaunce
fful manyaday but schortly þis is þe ende
Homward to rome þey schapyn hem to wende
This senatour repayreth wictorye
To romeward saylynge ful ryalye
And mette þe schyp dryuynge as seyth þe story
In which Custaunce sit pitously
No þyng knewe he what sche was ne why
Sche was in swich aray  ne sche wolde seye
Of hyre estat þow sche schulde deye


He bryngith hire to rome and to hise wyf  
He ȝaf hire and hire ȝonge sone also
And with þe senatour sche ledde hire lyf
Thus can oure lady bryngyn out of wo
Woful custaunce and manye a noþer mo
And long tyme dwellede sche in þat plase
In holye werkys euere as was hyre grace
This senatourys wyf hyre aunte was
But for al þat sche knew hyre neuere þe more
I wele no lengere taryen in þis cas
But to kyng alla which I spak of ȝore
That for hise wyf wepede and syghede sore
I wele retorne and lete I wele Custaunce
Vndyr þe senatourrys gouernaunce
Kyng Alla wich þat hadde hise modyr slayn
Vpon a day fil In swich repentaunce
That ȝif I schortely schulde telle and playn
To rome he comyth to receyue hese penaunce
And putte hym in þe popis ordenaunce
In high and logh and Ihesu crist besouȝte
fforȝeue hise wikke werkis þat he wrouȝte
The fame anon þour rome toun is born
How Alla kyng schal come in pilgrymage
By herberiourys þat wentyn here beforn
ffor which þe senatour as was þe vsage
Rod hym ageyn as was þe vsage
As wel to schewyn his magnificence
As to don any kyng a reuerence
Gret cher doth þis noble senatour  
To kyng alla and he to hym also
Euerych of hem doþ oþer gret honour
An that within a day or too


This senatour is to kyng Alla go
To feste and schortly ȝif I schal not lye
Custauncis sone wente in his cumpanye
Summen wolde seyn at þe request of Custaunce
This senatour hath lad þis child to feste
I ne may not tellyn euery circumstaunce
Be as be may þere was he at þe leste
But soth is þis þat at his moderys heste
Byforn Alla durynge þe metis space
This child stod lokynge in þe kyngis face
This Alla kyng hath of þe child gret wondyr
And to þe senatour he seyde anon
Whos is þat fayre child þat standis ȝondyr
I not quod he bi god and bi seynt Iohn
A modyr he hath but fadyr hath he non
That I of wot and schortly in a stounde
He tolde alla how þat þe child was founde
But god wot quod this senatour also
So verteuous a leuere in myn lyue
Ne saw I neuere as sche ne herde of mo
Of wordely wemen maydyn nor of wif
I dare wel seyn hire hadde leuere a knyf
Thurghout hyre brest þan ben a woman weke
þere is no man coude brynge hire to þe prikke
Now was þis child as lyk onto custaunce
As possible is a creatour to be
This alla hath þis face in remembraunce
Of dame custaunce and þeron musede he
Ȝif þat þe childis modyr were ouȝt sche
That is his wyf and pryuyly he sighte
And sped hym from þe table þat he myȝte


Parfay thouȝte he fantome is in myn hed  
I oghte deme of ryȝtful iugement
That in þe salte se myn wif is ded
And aftyr he made hise argument
What wot I if þat crist hath hire Isent
Myn wif be se as wel as he hire sente
To myn cuntre from þens þat sche wente
And aftyr non hom with þe senatour
Goth alla for to se þis wondyr chaunce
This senatour doth alla gret honour
And hastilyche he sente aftyr custaunce
But trustyth wel hire lyste not to daunce
Whan þat sche wiste wherfore was þat sonde
Oneþe vpon hire feet sche myȝte stonde
Whan Alla saw his wif fayre he hire grette
And wep þat it was routhe for to se
ffor at þe ferste lok he on hyre sette
He knewe wel verayly þat it was sche
And sche for sorwe as doumb stant as a tre
So was hire herte set in distresse
Whan sche remembrede hys vnkyndenesse
Twyes sche swounnyth in hise owene syghit
He wepte and hym excuseth pitously
Now god quod he and hise halwis bryȝte
So wisely on myn soule as haue mercy
That of ȝoure harm as gilteles am I
As is Mauryce myn sone so lyk ȝoure face
Ellis þe fend me feche out of þis place
Long was þe sobyng and þe bittere peyne
Er þat hire woful hertis myȝtyn cesse
Gret was þe pyte for to here hem pleyne
Thorgh whiche pleyntis gan hire wo encrese


I prey ȝow of myn labour to relese
I may nat telle here wo vntyl to morwe
I am so wery for to speke of sorwe
But finalli whan þat þe sorwe is wist  
That Alla giltles was of hire wo
I trowe an hunderede tymys ben þey kyst
And swich a blysse is þere betwen hem two
That saue þe ioye þat lastyth eueremo
There is non lyk þat any creature
Hath seyn or schal whil þe word wele dure
Tho preyede sche hire housbonde mekely
In relef of hire longe pitous peyne
That he wolde preye hire fadyr specially
That of his maieste he wolde enclyne
To vouchesaf sumday with hem to dyne
Sche preyede hym ek he schulde be no weye
Vnto hire fadyr no word of hire seye
Summen wolde seyn how þat þe child mauryce
Doth þis message vnto þis emperour
But as I gesse alla was not so nyce
To hym þat was of so souereyn honour
As he þat is of cristene folk þe flour
Sente any child but it is bet to deme
He wente him selue and so it may wel seme
This emperour hath grauntid gentyly
To come to dyner as he hym besouȝte
And wel rede I he lokede besily
Vpon þis child and on his douȝtyr thouȝte
Alla goth to hise in and as hym ouȝte
Arayede for þis feste in euery wyse
As fer forth as hise kunnynge may suffyse


The morwe cam and alla gan hym dresse
And ek his wif þis emperour to mete
And forth þey rede In ioye and in gladnesse
And whan sche saw hire fadyr in þe strete
Sche lyȝte adoun and fallyth hym to feete
ffadyr quod sche ȝoure ȝonge chyld Custaunce
Is now ful clene out of ȝoure remembraunce
I am ȝoure douȝty custaunce quod sche  
That whilhom han sent vnto surrye
It am I fadyr þat in þe salte se
Was put alone and dampned for to deye
Now goode fadyr mercy I ȝow preye
Sende me no more vnto to non hethenesse
But thanke myn lord here of his kyndenesse
Who can þe pytous ioye tellyn al
Bytwexe hem thre syn þey ben þus Imette
But of myn tale makyn an ende I schal
The day goth faste I wele no lengere lette
These glade folk to dyner þey ben sette
In ioye and blysse at dyner I lete hem dwelle
A thousent fold more þan I can telle
This child Maurice was sythe emperour
Mad bi þe pope and lyuede cristene lyf
To Cristis cherche he dede gret honour
But I lete alle hise storyis passyn by
Of Custaunce is myn tale specially
In þe olde romayn storyis may men fynde
Maurycis lyf I bere it not in mynde
This kyng Alla whan he hise tyme say
With his Custaunce his holy wif so swete
To ingelond ben þey come þe ryȝte way
Where as þey lyue In ioye and in quiete


But lytil while it lastyth I ȝow hete
Ioye of þis world for tyme wele not abyde
ffrom day to nyȝt it schaungith as þe tyde
Who lyuede euere in swich delyt a day
That sche ne menede outhir concyence
Or yre or talent or sumkenys afray
Enuye or pride or passioun or offence
I ne seye but for þis ende this sentence
That lytyl while in ioye and in plesaunce
Lastith þe ioye of alla with Custaunce
ffor deth þat takyth of high and low hise rente  
Whan passede was euene a ȝer as I gesse
Out of þe world þis kyng alla he hente
ffor whom Custaunce hath ful gret heuinesse
Now let vs preyen god his soule blysse
And dame Custaunce finally to seye
Toward þe toun goth hire weye
To rome is comyn þis holy creature
And fyndith hire frendis hole and sounde
Now is sche scapid al hire Auenture
And whan þat sche hire fadyr hath Ifounde
Doun on hire kneis fallyth sche to grounde
Wepynge for tendirnesse in herte blyþe
Sche heryeth god an hundered thousent sythe
In vertu and holy allemesse dede
They lyuyn alle and neuere asundyr wende
Thil deth departyth hem þis lyf þey leede
And faryth now wel myn tale is at an ende
Now Ihesu crist þat of his myȝt may sende
Ioye aftyr wo gouerne vs in hise grace
And kepe vs alle þat ben in þis place Amen
Experyment þough none auctoryte
Were in þis worlde is riȝt ynouȝe for me
To speke of woo þat ys in mariage
ffor lordynges siþen I twelfe yere was of age
Thanked by god þat ys eterne on lyue
Housbondes atte Chirche dore haue I hade fyue
Yf I so ofte myȝt haue wedded be
But alle were worþi men in her degre
But me was tolde certayne not longe agone ys
þat sithen cryste ne went nevere but onys
To weddynge in þe Cane of Galile
þat be þilke ensample tauȝt he me
þat I ne shulde wedded be but onys
Herke with a sharpe worde with þe nonys
By syde a welle Ihesu god and man
Spake in reprefe of þe Samarytan
Thou haste yhade v husbondes quod he
And þat ilke man þat nowe hathe the
Ys not þine husbonde þus sayde he certayne
What he mente þerby I can not sayne
Well but I axe why þe fyfte man
Was none housbonde to þe Samarytan
And herde telle in myne age
howe many myȝt she haue in mariage
  
Vpon þis nombre of diffinicion
Men may deuyne and glose vp and doun
But wele I wote expresse without lye
God bad vs wexe and multiplie
þat gentille text can I wele vndirstonde
Eke wele I wote he sayd myn husbonde
Schulde let ffadir and modir and take to me
But of none nombre mencion made he
Of Bygamye or of Octogamye
Whi shulde men of hit haue vilonye
Loke better þe wyse man kynge Salamon
I trowe he hade wyues mo þan on
Now wold god hit leffulle were to me  
To be refresshid half so ofte as he
Whiche yifte of god hade he for alle his wyues
No man þat hathe suche þat in þis world ys
God wote þis noble kynge as to my witte
The fyrst nyȝt hade many a mery fytte
With Iche of hem so wele was he a lyue
Blissed be god þat I haue weddid fyue
Welle come þe sixte whan þat euere he shalle
ffor siche I wille nouȝt kepe chaste in alle
What myne husbonde ys fro þe worlde gone
Some crysten man shalle wedde me anone
ffor þan þe Appostell seithe þat I am fre
To wedde a goddes half where hit likes me
he seyth þat to be weddid ys no synne
Bettere ys to be wedded þan to brenne
What recketh me þouȝe folke say vilonye
Of shrewed lameche and his Bygamye
I wote wele Abraham was an holy man
And Iacob eke as fer as I euere can
And eche of  hade wyues mo þan two
And many an othere man also
Where can ye say in eny manere age
þat vs god deffendid mariage
  
By expresse worde I prey you telle me
Or where comaundid he virgynyte
I wote as wele as ȝe hit ys no drede
The Apostill whan þat he speketh of Maydenhede
he sayd precept þerof hade he none
Men May consayle a woman to ben one
But consaylynge ys none comaundement
He putte hit in oure owen Iugement
ffor hade god commaunded Maydenhede
þan hade he dampned weddynge with þe dede
And certes yf þere were no sede ysowe
Virgynyte þan whereof shuld hit growe
Poule durste not comaunden atte leste  
A thynge of whiche his Mayster yaf hym none heste
þe dart ys set vpe for Virgynite
Chase who so may who so renneth best let see
But þis word is not take of euery wyght  
But þere as god lust ȝeue it of hise myȝt
I wot wel þat thapostele was a mayde
But natheles thogh þat he wrot and sayde
He wolde þat euery were swych as he
Al nys but cunseyl to virginite
And for to been a wyf he ȝaf me leue
Of indulgence so is it no repreue
To wedde me ȝif myn make deye
Withoute excepcioun of bygamye
Al were it good no woman for to touche
He mente as in his bed as in hyse couche
ffor peril is fer and tow thasemble
ȝe knowe what þis exsaumple may recemble
This is al and sum þat virginyte
More profitith þan weddyng in frelete
ffrelete clepe I ȝif̣ þat he and sche
Wolde leede al here lyf in chastite
I graunte it wel I haue non enuye
Thow maydynhed profere bigamye
  
Hem lykith to be clene body and gost
Of myn estat I nyl not make no bost
ffor wel ȝe wete a lord in hyse houshold
He hath nat euery vessel al of gold
Some ben of tre and don here lord seruyse
God clepith folk to hym in sundery wyse
And eueryche hath of god a propere ȝifte
Summe þis some þat as hym lestyth schyfte
Virginite 1is gret perfeccyoun1
And contynens ek with reson
But crist þat of perfeccioun is welle
Bad nat euery wyȝt schulde selle
Al þat he hadde and ȝeue it to þe pore
And in swich wise folwe hym and hese foore
He spak to hem þat wolde leue perfytly
And lordyngys by ȝoure leue þat am nat I
I wele bestowe þe flour of al myn age
In the artys and in þe freut of maryage
Telle me also to what conclusyoun  
Were membris made of generacioun
And for what profyt was a wyf Iwrouȝt
Trostyth ryȝt wel þey were nat mad for nouȝt
Glose ho so wele I seye vp and doun
That þey were makyd for purgacyoun
Of vryne boþe and thyngis smale
And ek to knowe a femel from a male
And for non oþer cause sey ȝe no
The experience wit wel it is nat so
So þat ȝe clerkis ben nat with me wrothe
I seye þis þat þey ben makede for boþe
That is to seye for offyse and for ese
Of engendereure þere we not god displese
Whi schuldyn men ellys in here bokis sette
That a man schal ȝilde to his wif hire dette
Now wherewith schulde he make hyse payement
If he ne vsede his instrument
  
Thanne were þey made vpon a creature
To purge vryne and for engendereure
But I sey not þat euery wyȝt is holde
That hath swich harneys as I of tolde
To gon and vse hem in engenderure
They schul nat take of chastite no cure
Cryst was a maydyn and schapyn as a man
And manye a seynt sithe þe world began
ȝit leuede þey euere in parfyt chastite
I nyl not enuye swych virginite
Let hem be bred of pure whete seed
And lat vs wyuys hote barli breed
And ȝit with barli bred mark telle can
That oure lord refroschid manye a man
In swich estat as god clepith vs
I wele perseuere I am nat precious
In wyfhod I wele vse myn instrument
As frely as myn makere hath it sent
ȝif I be dangerous god gif me sorwe
Myn housbonde schal it haue on eue and morwe
Whan þat hym lyste come forth and paye hise dette  
An housbonde wele I haue I nyl nat lette
Whiche schal be boþe myn detour and myn thral
And haue hise trybulacioun withal
Vpon hise flesch whil I am his wyf
I haue þe power durynge al myn lyf
Vpon hyse proper body and noght he
Ryght þus thapostele tolde it me
And bad oure housbondys forto loue vs wel
Al þis sentence me likyth euerydel
Vp sterte þe pardoūner and þat anon
Now dame quod he bi god and by seyn Iohn
ȝe ben a noble prechour in þis cas
I was abute to wedde a wyf allas
What schulde I it beye on myn flesch so dere
ȝit hadde I leuere wedde no wif to ȝere
  
Abyde quod sche myn tale is nat begunne
Nay þou schat drynkyn of anoþer tunne
Or þan I go schal sauoure werse þan ale
And whan þat I haue told forth myn tale
Of trybulacioun þat is in maryage
Of which I am expert in al myn age
This is to seyn myn self hath ben þe wippe
Thanne mayȝt þou chese wheþer þou wolt skyppe
Of þat tunne þat I schal abroche
Be war of it er þou to nygh aproche
ffor I schal telle ensample mo þan ten
Who so þat wele nat be war by oþere men
By hym schul oþere men corectid be
The same wordys wrytht protholome
Rede it in hise almagestis and take it þere
Dame I wolde preye ȝif ȝoue wil it were
seyde þis pardounner as ȝe began
Tellyth forth ȝoure tale sparyth nan
And tellith vs ȝynge men of ȝoure praptik
Gladly sire sithe it may ȝow lyk
But ȝit I preye to al þis cumpaynye
If þat I speke aftyr myn fantasye
As takyth nat a gres þat I seye  
ffor myn entent is but for to pleye
Now sere now wele I telle forth myn tale
As euere mote I drynkyn wyn or ale
I schal sey soth of housbondis þat I hadde
As thre of hem were goode and thre were badde
The thre men were goode and rych and olde
Oneþe myȝt þey þe statut holde
In which þat þey were boundyn on to me
ȝe wete wel what I mene of þis parde
As helpe me god I laughe whan I thynke
How pytously on nyȝt I made hem to swynke
But be myn fey I tolde of it no stor
They haddyn me ȝeuyn hire lond and hire tresor
  
Me nedede not do lengere diligence
To wynne hire loue and don hire reuerence
They louede me so wel by god aboue
That I ne told no deynte of here loue
As wys woman wele sette hire euere in on
To gete hire loue þere as sche hath non
But sythe I haue hem holy in myn hond
And sithe þey han me ȝeuyn al here lond
What schulde I take hed hem for to plese
But ȝif it were for myn profyt and myn ese
I sette hem so awerke be myn fey
That manye a nyȝt þey sunge weyleawey
The bakon was nat fet for hem I trowe
That some men han in exces at dunmowe
I gouernede hem so wel aftyr my lawe
That eche of hem was blysful and ful fawe
To brynge me gay þyng from þe feyre
They were ful glad whan I spak tyl hem fayre
ffor god it wot I schid hem spitously
Now herkenyth how I bar me properly
ȝe wise wyuys þat kunne vndyrstonde
Thus schul ȝe speke and bere hem wrong on honde
ffor half so boldely can þere no man
Swere and lye as can a woman
I seye it nat be wyuys þat been wyse  
But ȝif it be whan þey hym mysavise
A wis wif ȝif þat sche can hire good
Schal bere hym on hande þe cou is wod
And take witnesse of hire owene mayde
Of hire asent but herkenyth how I seyde
Syre olde caynard is þis þyn aray
Whi is myn neyheborys wif so gay
Sche is honourede euere al þere sche goth
I sitte at hom and haue no thryfty cloth
What dost þou at myn neyhebouris hous
Is sche so fayr and þow so amerous
  
What rounne ȝe with oure maydenys benedicite
Sire olde lechour lat ȝoure iapis be
And ȝif I haue a gossib or a frend
Withoutyn gilt þou chidist as a fend
ȝif þat I walke or pleye vntyl hise hous
þou comyst hom as dronkyn as a mous
And prechist on þyn bench with euele pref
þou seyst to me it is a gret myschef
To wedde a poore woman for costage
And ȝif sche be ryche and of hey parage
þanne seyst þou it is a turmeterye
To suffere hire pryde and malencolye
And ȝif þat sche be fayr þou veray knaue
þou seyst þat euery holour wele hire haue
Sche may no while in chastite on byde
That is asayled on eche asyde
þou seyst þat some folk desyryn vs for rychesse
Summe for oure schap some for oure fayrenesse
And some for sche can synge and daunce
And some for gentilesse and some for dalyaunce
Some for hire handis and for hire armys smale
Thus goth al to þe deuyl be þyn tale
Thow seyst men may nat kepe a castel wal
It may so longe asaylede ben oueral
And ȝif þat sche be foul þou seyst þat sche
Coueytith euery man þat sche may se
ffor as a spaynel sche wil on hym lepe  
Til þat sche fynde sum man hire to schepe
Ne non so grey gos þat goth in þe lake
As þou seyst wele be withoute a make
And seyst it is an hard þyng for to welde
A thyng þat no man wele hise thankis helde
Thow seyst horel whan þou gost to bedde
How þat no wys man nedyth for to wedde
Ne no man þat tendyth onto heuene
With wylde thundyr dynt in fery leuene
  
Mote þyn wekede neke be tobroke
þou seyst þat droppynge housis and ek smoke
And chydyng wyf makyth men to fle
Out of here owene hous a benedicite
What eylyth swich an old man to chyde
þou seyst þat we wyuis wele oure vicis hyde
Til we ben fast and þanne we wele hem schewe
Wel may þat ben a prouerbe of a schrewe
þou seyst þat oxsyn Assis hors and houndys
þey ben asayed at dyuerse stoundys
Basenys lauourys er þan men hem beye
sponys and stolis and alle swich husbondrye
And also cloþis pottys and aray
But folk of wyuys makyn non asay
Til þey ben weddit olde dotard schrewe
Thanne seyst þou we wele oure vicis schewe
Thou seyst also þat it displeseþ me
But ȝif þat þou wilt preyse myn beute
And but þou poure alwey in myn face
And clepe me fayre dame in euery place
And but þou make a feste on þat day
þat I was born and make me frosch and gay
And but þou do to myn noryce honour
And to myn chaumberere withinne myn bour
And to mynne faderys folkys and mynne alyes
Thus seyst þou olde barel ful of lyis
And ȝit of oure apprentys Iankyn
ffor his scrip here schynynge as gold fyn
And for he squyeryth me vp and doun  
ȝit hast þou cauȝt fals suspecioun
I nyl hym not þow  were ded to morwe
But telle me whi hydistow with sorwe
The keyes of myn cheste al day from me
It is myn good as wel as þyn parde
What wenyst þou to make an ydiot of oure dame
Now by þat lord þat callede is seynt Iame
  
Thow schat not boþe þow þou were wood
Ben maystyr of myn body and ek of myn good
That on þou schat forgon maugery þyn Iyen
What helpith it of me te enquere or spyen
I trowe þou woldist louke me in þyn cheste
Thow schuldist sey wyf go where þe leste
Take ȝoure disport I nyl leue no talys
I knowe ȝow for a trewe wif dame alis
We loue no man þat take kep or charge
Where þat we gon we wele ben at oure large
Of alle men blyssede mote he bee
The wyse Astrolages dann Protholomee
That say þis prouerbe in his almageste
Of alle men his wisdom is þe heyeste
That rekyth neuere ho hath þe world in honde
By þis prouerbe þou schat vndyrstonde
Haue þou Inow what thar þe reche or care
How meryly þat oþere folkys fare
ffor serteyn olde dotard by ȝoure leue
ȝe schal haue queynte ryȝt Inow at eue
He is a gret nygard þat wolde werne
A man to lyȝte a candele at his lanterne
He schal haue neuere þe lesse lyȝt parde
Haue þou Inow þe thar not pleyne þe
þou seyst also þat ȝif we make vs gay
With cloþynge and with precious aray
That it is peryl of oure chastyte
And ȝit with sorwe þou muste enforse þe
And seye þese wordis in þe apostelys name
In abite mad with chastite and schame
ȝe wemen schul aparayle ȝow quod he  
And not in trussede her and gay parre
As pereles ne with gold ne with cloþis ryche
Aftyr þyn tix ne aftyr rubryche
I wol not werke as meche as a gnat
þou seydist þis þat I was lyk a cat
  
ffor who so wolde senge a cattis skyn
Thanne wolde þe cat dwelle in his In
And ȝif þe cattis skyn be slyk and gay
Sche wil not dwelle in house half a day
But forth sche wele er any day be dawyd
To schewe hire skyn and gon a catirwawid
This is to seye ȝif I be gay sere schrewe
I wele renne aboute myn borel to schewe
Sire olde fol what eylyth þe to aspien
Thow þou preye argus with hise C eyen
To be myn warde cors as he can best
In feyth he schal nat kepe me but me lest
ȝit I coude make his berd so mote I the
þou seydist ek þat þere ben thyngis thre
Theche thyngis trobelyn al þis erþe
And þat no whit may endure þe ferþe
O leue sire schrewe Ihesu schorte þyn lyf
ȝit prechist þou and seyst þat an hateful wyf
Irekenede is for on of þese myschauncis
Ben þere non oþere of þese recemblauncis
That ȝe may likene ȝoure parabele to
But ȝif a sely wif be on of þo
þou likkenyst womanys loue to helle
To barayne lond þere no watyr may dwelle
þou likenyst it also to wildefer
The more it brennyth þe more it hath desyr
To consumme euery þynk þat brent wele be
Thow seyst ryȝt as wermys consume a tre
Ryȝt so a wif distroyeþ hire husbonde
That knowyn þey þat ben to wyuys bonde
Lordyngis ryȝt þus as ȝe han vndyrstonde
Bar I stifly myn olde housbonde on honde
That þus þey seydyn in here dronkenes  
And al was fals but þat I tok witnes
On Iankyn and on myn nece also
O lord þe peyne I dede hem and þe wo
  
fful gilteles by godys swete pyne
ffor as an hors coude bite and whine
I coude pleyne and ȝit was in þe gilt
Or ellis I hadde ofte tymys ben spilt
Who so come fyrst to melle fyrst grynt
I pleynede fyrst so was oure werre stent
They were ful glad to excuse hem blyue
Of thyng þey neuere agilt in al here lyue
And of wenchis wolde I bere hem on honde
Whan þat for sek oneþe myȝte stonde
ȝit tekelede I his herte for þat he
Wende þat I hadde had of hym gret chirte
I sey þat al myn walkynge out be nyȝte
Is for to espien wenchis þat he dyȝte
Vndyr þat colour hadde I manye a murthe
ffor al swych wit is ȝeuyn vs in oure burthe
Deseyt wepynd spynnyng god hath ȝeue
To wemen kyndely whan þat þey may lyue
And þus of on thyng I awaunte me
At þe ende I hadde þe betere in eche degre
Be sleyghe or forse or sum manere thynge
As by continuel murmure and grochynge
Nameli on bedde hadde þey myschaunce
There wolde I chide and don hem non plesaunce
I wolde no lengere in þe bed abyde
ȝif þat I felte his arm ouyr myn syde
Til he hadde mad his raunsum on to me
Thanne wolde I suffere hym to don hise nysete
And þerfore euery man hise tale telle
Wyn ho so may for al is for to selle
With emty hond men may none haukys lure
ffor wynnyng wolde I al hise lust endure
And make me a feynede apetit
And ȝit in bacoun hadde I neuere delit
þat made me euere þat I wolde hym chyde  
ffor þow þe pope hadde sete by hyse syde
  
I nolde hym spare at hise owene boord
ffor by myn trouthe I quitte hym word for word
As help me veray god omnypotent
Thow I schulde make now myn testement
I ne owe hem nat a word þat it nys quit
I brouȝte it so aboute by myn wit
That þey muste ȝeue it vp as for þe beste
Or ellis hade we neuere ben in reste
ffor þow he lokede as a wood lyoun
ȝit he schulde fayle of hise conclusioun
Thanne wolde I seye goode loue take kep
How mekely lokyth wilkyn oure schep
Come neer myn spouse lat me ba þyn scheke
ȝe schul be al pacient and meke
And haue a swete spicede concience
Sithin ȝe preche so of Iobes pacience
Sufferith alwey sithe ȝe so wel can preche
And but ȝe don certeyn we schul ȝow teche
That it is fayr to haue a wyf in pes
On of vs to muste bouwe douteles
And seyth a man is more resonable
þan woman is ȝe muste be sufferable
What eylyth ȝow thus to groche and grone
Is it for ȝe wolde han myn queynte alone
Whi take it al lo haue it euerydel
Petyr Ischrewe ȝow but ȝe loue it wel
ffor ȝif I wolde selle myn belechose
I coude walke as frosch as ony rose
But I wele kepe it for ȝoure owene toth
ȝe ben to blame by god I seye ȝow soth
Sweche manere of wordis hadde we on honde
Now wele I speke of myn fourte housbonde
Myn fourte housbonde was a reuelour
This is to seyne he hadde a paramour
And I was ȝong and ful of ragerye
Styborne and strong and Ioly as a pye
  
Wel coude I daunce to an harpe smale  
And synge Iwis as ony nyghtyngale
Whan I hadde dronke a drauȝt of swete wyn
Metullius þe foule clerk þe swyn
That with a staf berafte his wif hire lyf
ffor sche drank wyn and I hadde been his wif
He schulde nat a dauntid me from drynk
And aftyr wyn on venus muste I thynk
ffor al so sykyr as cold engenderyth hayl
A lycorous mouth muste han a licorous tayl
In woman vinolent is no defence
This knowyn lechourys bi experyence
But lord cryst whan it remembryth me
Vpon myn thout and on myn iolyte
It tykelith me aboute myn herte rote
Vnto þis day it doth myn herte bote
That I haue had myn world as In myn tyme
But age allas þat al wole vndyrmyne
Hath me bereft myn beute and myn pith
Let go farewel þe deuyl go þerwith
The flour is gon þere is no more to telle
The bren as I best can now muste I selle
But ȝit to ben merye wele I euere fonde
Now wele I telle of myn fourte husbonde
I seye I hadde in herte gret dispit
That he of ony oþer hadde delyt
But he was quit by god and be seynt Ioce
I made hym of þe same wode a croce
Nat of myn body in no foul maner
But serteynly I made folk swich cher
That in hise owene grese I made hym frye
ffor pure angir and for Ielouye
Bi god in erþe he was in purgatorie
ffor whiche I hope his soule be in glorie
ffor god it wot he sat ful ofte and song
Whan þat his schon ful bittyrly him wrong
  
There was no wyȝt but god and he þat wiste
In manye wise how sore I hym twyste
He deyede whan I cam from Ierusalem  
And lith Igraue vndir þe rode bem
Al Is his toumbe not so coryous
As was þe sepulcre of hym daryus
Whiche þat Arpelles wrouȝte so subtily
It is but wast to burye hem so precyously
Lat hym fare wel god ȝeue his soule reste
He is now in hise graue and in his cheste
Now of myn fifte husbonde wele I telle
God lete his soule neuere come in helle
And ȝit was he to me þe moste schrewe
That fele I on mynne rebis alle bewrewe
And euere schal vnto myn endyng day
But in oure bed he was so frosch and gay
And þerwithal wel coude he me glose
Whan þat he wolde haue myn belechose
That þow he hadde me betyn on euery bon
He coude wynne myn loue aȝen anon
I trowe I louede hym beste for þat he
Was of his loue dangerous to me
We wemen haue ȝif I schal nat lye
In þis matyre a queynte fantasye
That what þyng we may nat lyȝtely haue
þeraftyr wele most crye and craue
fforbede vs thyng þat desyre we
Presse on vs faste and þanne wele we fle
With daunger oute we oure chaffare
Gret pres in market makyth dere ware
And to good chep is holde of lytyl prys
This knowyth euery woman þat is wys
Myn fyfte husbonde god his soule blysse
Whiche þat I tok for loue and no rychesse
He sumtyme was a clerk of oxsene forde
And hadde left skole and wente at hom to borde
  
With myn gossib dwellynge in oure toun
God haue hire soule hire name was alysoun
Sche knew myn herte and ek myn pryuite
Bet þan oure paryche prest so mote I the
To hire bewreyede I myn conseyl al  
ffor hadde myn husebonde pissede on a wal
Or don ony thyng þat schulde a cost his lyf
To hire and to anoþer worthi wyf
And to myn nece þat I louede wel
I wolde haue tolde hise conseyl euerydel
And so I dede ful ofte god it wot
That made hise face ofte red and hot
ffor verray schame and blamede hym self þat he
Hadde told me so gret a pryuyte
And so befel þat onys in a lente
So ofte tyme I to myn gossib wente
ffor euere þat I louede to be gay
And for to walke in marsch auerylle and may
ffrom hous to hous to heryn sundery talis
That Iankyn clerk and myn gossib dame Alis
And I myn self vp to þe feldis wente
Myn housbonde was at lundene al þat lente
And I hadde þe betere leyser for to pleye
And for to se and ek for to be seye
Of lusty folk what wyste I where myn grace
Whas schape for to be or in what place
Therfore I made mynne visitaciounnys
To vigilis and to procesciounnys
To prechyngis ek and to pylgrymagis
To pleyes of myrakelis and of mariagis
And werede vpon myne scarlet gites
These wormes these mothis and these mytis
Vpon myn peryl frete hem neuere a del
And wost þou why for they were vsede wel
Nowe wele I telle forth what happede me
I seye þat in the feldys walkede we
  
Tyl trewely we haddyn swich a dalyaunce
This clerk and I þat of myn puruyaunce
I spak to hym and seyde how þat he
ȝif I were wedewe he schulde wedde me
ffor serteynly I seye for no bobaunce
ȝit was I neuere withoute puruyaunce
Of mariage and more thyngis eek  
I holde a mousys herte not worth a leek
That hath but on hole to sterte to
And that fayle thanne is al Ido
I bere hym on honde he enchauntede me
Myn dame taughte me þat sotylete
And ek I seyde I mette of hym al nyȝt
He wolde a slayn me as I lay vp ryȝt
And al myn bed was ful of veray blood
But ȝit I hope þat he schal do me good
ffor blood betokenyth gold as me was tauȝt
And al was fals I dremede of it ryght nauȝt
But I folwede ay myn damys lore
As wel of this as of oþere thyngis more
But now syre lat se what schal I seyn
Aha by god I haue myn tale ageyn
What that myn husbonde was on bere
I weep and made a sory chere
As wyuys motyn for it is vsage
And with myn couerechef couerede myn visage
But for þat I was purueyed of a make
I wepte but smal and þat I vndyrtake
To cherche was myn husbond o born on morwe
With negheboris þat for hym madyn sorwe
And Iankyn oure klerk was on of thoo
As help me god whan that I saw hym goo
Aftyr þe beere me thoughte he hadde a payre
Of leggis and feet so clene and fayre
That al myn herte I ȝaf vnto his hold
He was I trowe twenty wyntyr old
  
And I was fourty ȝif I schal sey sooth
And ȝit I hadde alway a coltys toth
Gattothid I was and that becam me wel
I hadde the prente of seynt peterys sel
As help me god I was a lusty on
ffayr and ryche and frosch and wel begon
And trewely as myn husbondys toldyn me
I hadde the beste quoniam that myȝte be
ffor sertis I am al venerient  
In felynge and myn herte is marcient
Venus me ȝaf myn lust myn licorousnesse
And mars ȝaf me myn hardynesse
Myn ascendent was taur and mars ther Inne
Allas allas that euere loue was synne
I folwede ay myn Inclynacyoun
By vertu of myn constolacioun
That made me that I coude nat withdrawe
Myn chambere of venus from a good felawe
ȝit haue I Martes mark vpon myn face
And also in anothyr preue place
ffor god so wis be myn sauacyoun
I ne lewede neuere by non discrecyoun
But euere folwede myn apetit
