Al were he schort or long or blak or whȝt
I tok no kep so þat he lykede mee
How pore ne ek o what degree
What schal I sey but at þe monethis ende
This Ioly clerk Iankyn that was so hynde
Hath wedede me with gret solempnetee
And to hym ȝaf I al that lond and fee
That euere was me ȝeuyn þere byfoore
But aftyrward me repentede sone therfore
He nolde suffere no thyng of myn lyst
But onys he smot me with hyse fyst
ffor I rente onys out of hyse bok a lef
That for the strok myn ere wex al def
  
Styborne I was as a leonesse
And of myn tunge a veray Iangeleresse
And walke I wolde as  hadde don byforn
ffrom hous to hous althow he hadde it sworn
ffor whiche ofte tymys he wolde preche
And me olde romayn geestys teche
How he symplycious Gallus lafte his wyf
And hire for sok for terme of al his lyf
Not but for o poynt he hyre say
Lokynge out of hyse dore vpon a day
Anothir Romayn tolde he by name  
That for hise wif was at a somer game
Withoutyn hyse wetynge he forsok hire eke
And thanne wolde he vpon hise bible seeke
That ilke prouerbe of ecclesiaste
Where he comaundyth and forbedyth faste
Men schal not suffere here wyvis to roule aboute
Thanne wolde he seye thus withoutyn doute
Whoso byldyth hise hous al of salwys
And prikyth hyse blynde hors ouere þe falewis
And sufferith his wyf go sekyn halwys
Is worthi to been hangyn on the galwis
But al for nouȝt I sette nat an hawe
Of hise prouerbis ne of hise olde sawe
Ne I nulde of hym corectede be
I hate hym that mynne vicis tellyn me
And so don mo god wot than I
This made hym holde me wood al outerely
I nolde forbere hym in no manere cas
Now wele I sey ȝow soth by seynt Thomays
Whi that I rente out of hise bok a lef
ffor whyche he smot me that I was def
He hadde a bok that gladly nyȝt and day
ffor his disport he wolde rede alway
He clepede it valerye and theofraste
At which bok he low ful faste
  
And ek he seyde that sumtyme there was a clerk at rome
A cardenale that hyȝt Ierome
That made a bok aȝen Iouynian
In whiche bok þere was ek Tertulan
Crisippus Tortula and Helowys
That was abbesse not fer from Parys
And ek the parabele of Salamon
Ouydis art and bokys many on
And alle these were boundyn In on volome
And euery day and nyȝt was hyse custome
Whan he hadde leyse and vacacyoun
ffrom oþere wordely ocupacyoun
To redyn on hise bok of wekede wyuys  
He knew of hem mo legendys and lyuys
Than ben of goode wyuys in the byble
ffor trostyth wel it is an Impossible
That any clerk schulde speke good of wyuys
But ȝif it be of holye seyntis lyuys
Ne of non othere woman neuere þe mo
Who peyntede þe lyoun tel me who
Bi god ȝif women haddyn wretyn storyis
As clerkis han with inne here oratoryis
They wolde a wrete of men more wekedenesse
Than al þe Mark of adam may redresse
The chylderyn of mercurye and of venus
Ben in hyre werkys wol contraryous
Mercurye louyth wysdom and science
And venus louyth riot and dispence
And for hire dyuerse dispocicioun
Eche fallyth in oþeris exsaltacyoun
And þus wot god Mercurye is desolat
In Pisses where Mercurye is exaltat
And venus fallyth where Mercurye is reysed
Therfore no woman of no klerk is preysed
The clerk whan he is old and may not do
Of venus werkys worth hyse olde scho
  
Thanne sit he doun and wryt in hise dotage
That wemen kunne not kepe here maryage
But now to purpos why I tolde the
That I was betyn for a bok pardee
Vpon a nyȝt Iankyn that was oure syre
Radde on his bok as he sat by the fyre
Of Eua fyrst that for hyre wikkedenes
Was al mankynde brouȝt to wrechedenes

That boughte vs with his herte blode agayne
Lo here expresse of women Maye ye ffynde
That women was the losse of All Mankynde  
Tho radde he me how sampson loste hyse heris
Slepynge his leman kitte hem with hyre scherys
Thorgh whych tresoun loste he bothe hyse eyen
Tho radde he me ȝif I schal nat lyen
Of ercules and of hyse dyanyre
That causede hym to sette hym selue a fyre
No thyng forgat he the care and the wo  
That socrates hadde with hyse wyuys two
How Exantippa caste pis vpon his hed
This sely man sat stylle as he were deed
He wypede his hed no more durste he seyn
But er thundyr stynte þere comyth a reyn
Of phasippa that was the queen of Crete
ffor schrewedenesse hym thouȝte the tale swete
ffy spek na more it is a gresely thyng
Of hire horrible lust and hire lykyng
Of clitemysta for hire lecherye
That falsely maade hire husbonde for to deye
He radde it with ful good deuocioun
He tolde me ek for what occasyoun
Amphiorax at thebes loste his lyf
Myn husbonde hadde a legende of his wyf
Eryphilem þat for an Ouche of gold
Hath priuyly on to þe grekys told
  
Where þat hyre husbonde hidde hym in a place
ffor whiche he hadde at thebes sory grace
Of lyma tolde he me and of lucye
Thy bothe made here housbondis for to dye
That on for loue that oþer for hate
Lyma hire housbonde on an euyn late
Enpoysounede hath for þat sche was his fo
Lucya lykerous louede hyre housbonde so
That he schulde alwey on hire thynke
Sche ȝaf hym swich a manere loue drynke
That he was ded er it was by þe morwe
And þus algatys housbondis haddyn sorwe
Thanne tolde he me how on latymyus
Compleynede to his felawe Arryus
That in hyse gardyn growede swych a tre
On whiche he seyde þat his wyuys thre
Hangede hem self for herte despitous
O leue brothir quod this Arryus
ȝif me a plante of that blyssede tre
And in myn gardyn schal it plauntede be
Of lattere date of wyuys þanne he radde  
That some han slayn here housbondis in here bedde
And leet hire lectour dyȝte hire al þe nyȝt
Whils þat þe cors lay in þe flor vpryȝt
And some han dryue a nayl in here brayn
Whils þat þey slepte and þus þey han hem slayn
Some han ȝeue hem poysoun in here drynk
He spak more harm than herte may bethynk
And þerwithal he knew mo prouerbis
Than in this world þere growe gres or erbis
Bet is quod he þat thyn habitacioun
Be with a lyoun or a foul dragoun
Than with a waman vsynge for to chyde
Betere is quod he hye in þe rof abyde
Than with a wekede woman doun in an hous
They ben so wekke and so contraryous
  
They hatyn that here housbondys louyn ay
He seyde a woman caste hire schame away
Whan sche caste of hire smok and ferþere mo
A fayr woman but sche be chast also
Is lik a golde ryng in a sowis nose
Ho wolde wene or ho wolde suppose
The wo that in myn herte was and pyne
And I saw þat he wolde neuere fyne
But redyn on hise cursede bok al nyȝt
Al sodeynly thre leuys haue I plyȝt
Out of his bok as he sat ful meke
And with myn fist so tok I hym on þe cheke
That in oure fyre he fyl bakward adoun
And he vp stirte as doth a wood lyoun
And with his fyst he smot me on the hed
That In the flor I lay as I were ded
And whan he saw how stylle I lay
He was agast and fledde away
Til at þe laste out of myn swow I breyde
O hast þou sleyn me thef I seyde
And þus for myn lond wilt þou mordere me
Er I be ded ȝit wele I kysse the
And ner he cam and knelede fayre adoun  
And seyde myn dere sistyr alysoun
Als helpe me god I schal þe neuere smyte
That I haue don It is thyn self to wyte
ffor ȝeue it me and þat I þe beseke
And ȝit eftsonys I hitte hym on the cleke
And seyde thef þus meche I may me wreke
Now wele I deye I may no lengere speke
But at þe laste with meche care and wo
We fille acordit by oure seluyn two
He ȝaf me al þe brydyl in myn hond
To haue gouernauns of hous and lond
And of his tunge and of his hond also
And made hym to brenne his bok ryȝt þo
  
And whanne I hadde Igetyn on to me
By maysterye al þe souereyntee
Thanne he seyde myn owene trewe wyf
Do as ȝe leste for terme of al ȝoure lyf
Keep thyn honour and thyn estat
Aftyr þat day we ne haddyn neuere debat
God help me so I was to hym as kynde
As ony wif from denmark vnto Inde
And as trewe and so was he to me
I preye to god þat sit in mageste
So blysse his soule for his mercy dere
Now wele I seye myn tale ȝif ȝe wele here
The frere low whan he hadde herd al this
Now dame quod he also haue I Ioye or blis
This is a long preamble of a tale
And whan þe somnour herde þe frere gale
Lo quod the sumnour bi goddys armys too
A frere wele entirmete hym euere mo
Lo goode men a flye and ek a frere
Wele falle in euery disch and matere
What spekyst þou of perambulacioun
What amble or trotte or pes or go sit doun
þou lettyst oure desport in þis matiere
ȝa wilt þou so syre somnour quod þe frere
Now by myn fey I schal er þat I go  
Telle of a sumnour a tale or too
That alle þe folk schul law he in þis place
Now ellis frere I beschrewe thyn face
Quod this sumnour and I beschrewe me
But ȝif I telle talis too or thre
Of freris er I come to Sidyngborne
That I schal make þyn herte for to moorne
  
ffor wel I wot þyn pacience is goon
Oure ost cryede pees and þat anon
And seyde lat þe woman telle hire tale
ȝe fare as folk dronke were of ale
Doth dame tellyth forth ȝoure tale and þat is best
Al redy sire quod sche ryght at ȝoure lest
ȝif I haue lycens of þis worþi frere
ȝis dame telle forth and I schal here
IN olde dayis of kyng Arthour
Of whiche þat brytons spekyn gret honour
Al was this lond ful fyld of fayrye
The elf quene wyth hire cumpanye
Dauncede ful ofte in manye a grene mede
This was the olde opynyoun as I rede
I speke of manye hunderede ȝeris ago
But now can no man se eluys mo
ffor now the charite and þe prayeris
Of lymytouris and of oþere holy frerys
That serchyn euery lond and euery strem
As thikke as motys in þe sone bem
Blessen halles chaumbery kichenys bourys
Ceteis borwys castelis hyghe tourys
Thropes bernys  Schipnes dayryis
That makyth that þere ben no fayryis
ffor þere as wont was for to walke an elf
There walkyth now þe lymytour hym self
In vndirmelys and in morwenyngis
And seyth hyse matynys and hyse holye thyngis
As he goth in hyse lymytacioun
Wemen mowe go sauely vp and doun
In euery bussch and vndyr euery tree
There is nower non Incubus but he
And he wele don hym non dishonour
And so befel þat this kyng Arthour
Hadde in his hous a ryche bacheler
That on a day cam rydynge from reuer
  
And happede alone as sche was born
He saw a mayde cam rydynge hym byforn
Of whiche maydyn anon maugry hire hed
By veray forse byrafte he hire maydynhed
ffor which apprecioun was swych clamour
And swych pursut to kyng arthour
That dampnede was the knyȝt for to be ded
By cours of lawe and schulde a lost hyse heed
Perauenture swich was the statute þo
But that þe queen and oþere ladyis moo
So longe preyedyn the kyng of grace  
Tyl he his lyf grauntede at þat place
And ȝaf hym to the queen at hire wille
To chese wheþer sche wolde hym saue or spille
The queen thankede þe kyng with al hyre myȝt
And aftyr this þus spak sche to þe knyȝt
Whan sche saw hyre tyme vpon a day
Thow stondist ȝit quod sche in swich aray
That of thyn lyf  hast no surete
I graunte þe lyf ȝif þou canst telle me
What thyng ist that wemen most desyryn
Bewar and kep thyn neke bon from yryn
And ȝif þou canst not telle me anon
ȝit wele I ȝeue þe leue for to goon
A twelvemonyth and a day to lere
An answere sufficiaunt in this matire
And surete wele I haue er þat þou pace
Thyn body for to ȝildyn in þis place
Wo was this knyȝt and sorwefully he sikede
But ȝit may he nat don as hym lykede
And at þe laste he ches hym for to weende
And come aȝen ryȝt at þe ȝerys ende
With swich answere as god wolde hym purueye
And takyth his leue and wendyth forth hyse weye
And sekyth euery hous and euery place
Where as he hopith to fynde grace
  
To lernyn what thyng wemen louyn most
But he ne coude aryuyn In no cost
Where as he myȝte fynde in this matyre
Two wightis acordyn in fyre
Some men seydyn women louyn best rychesse
Some men seyde honour some iolynesse
Some men seyde ryche aray some lust in bedde
And ofte tyme be wedewe and ofte Iwedde
Some men seyde oure herte is most Iesed
Whan þat we been Iflatered and Iplesed
He goth ful nygh þe sothe I nyl not lye
A man schal wynne vs best with flaterye
And with attendaunce and besynesse  
Be we Ilymyd boþe more and lesse
And some men seyn þat we louyn best
ffor to be fre and do ryȝt as vs lest
And þat no man repreue vs of oure vice
But seye þat we be wys and no thyng nyse
ffor trewely þere is non of vs alle
ȝif ony wyȝt wele clawe vs on the galle
That we nolde kyke for he seyth vs soth
Asay he schal fynde it þat so doth
ffor be we neuere so vicious withinne
We wele be holde wis and clene of synne
And some seyn that gret loue haue we
ffor to ben holde wyse and secre
And in on purpos stedefastly to dwelle
And not be wreye thyng þat men vs telle
But þat tale nys not worth a rake stele
Parde we wemen can nothyng hele
Witnesse of Mida wil ȝe here þe tale
Ouyde amongis oþere thyngis smale
Seyde Mida hadde vndyr hyse longe herys
Growynge on his hed two assis erys
The whiche vice he hyde as he best myghte
fful subtyly from euery manys syȝte
  
That saue his wyf þere wiste of it no mo
He louede hyre most and trostid to hyre also
He preyede hyre þat to no cryature
Sche schulde telle of his disfygure
Sche swor hym nay for al this world to wynne
Sche nolde not do þat vilany or synne
Go make hyre husbonde to haue so foul a name
Sche nele it telle for hyre owene schame
But neuereþeles hire thouȝte þat sche dyde
That sche so longe a conseylde hyde
Hire thouȝte it swal so sore aboute hyre herte
That nedely sum word muste asterte
And sythe sche durste telle it to no man
Doun to a mareys faste by sche ran
Tyl sche cam þere hire herte was a fyre  
And as a bitore bumbith in þe myre
Sche leyde hyre mouth to þe watyr adoun
Bewrey me not þou watyr with thyn soun
Quod sche to þe I telle it and no mo
Myn husbonde hath longe erys too
Now is al myn herte hol now is it oute
I myȝte no lengere kepe it out of doute
Here may ȝe se þow we no tyme abyde
ȝit out mote it we can no conseyl hyde
The remenaunt of þe tale ȝif ȝe wele here
Rede ouyde and þere mowe ȝe it leere
This knyȝt of which myn tale is specyally
Whan he saw he myȝte not come þerby
This is to seye what wemen louyn most
Withinne his brest full sorwefully was þe gost
But hom he goth he myȝte not soiorne
The day was come that homward muste he turne
And In hyse wey as happede hym to ryde
In al hise care vndyr a forest syde
Where as he saw vpon a daunce go
Of ladyis foure and twenty and ȝit mo
  
Toward þis dauns he drow ful ȝerne
In hope þat sum wisdam schulde he lerne
But serteyn fully er he cam ther
Vanysschid was the daunce he nyste wher
No cryateure saw he þat bar lyf
Saue on þe grene he saw syttynge a wyf
A foulere wyȝt þere may no man devyse
Aȝens þis knyȝt this olde whiȝt gan ryse
And seyde syre knyȝt here forth lyth no weye
Telle ȝe me what ȝe seke be ȝoure feye
Perauenture þe betere may it be
These olde folk can moche thyng quod sche
Myn leue modyr quod this knyght serteyn
I ne am but deed but ȝif þat I can seyn
What thyng ist þat wemen most desyre
Koude ȝe me wische I wolde quyte ȝoure hyre
Plyghte me þyn treuth in myn hond quod sche  
The nexte thyng that I require the
Thow shalt it do ȝif it be in þy myght
And I wele telle it ȝow er it be nyght
Haue her myn trouthe quod þe knyght I graunte
Thanne quod sche I dar me wel avaunte
Thyn lyf is saf I wele stonde þerby
Vpon myn lyf þe quen wele seye as I
Lat se which is þe proudest of hem alle
That weryth on a couerechief or a calle
Tha dar sey nay of þat I schal the teche
Lat vs go forth with oute lengere speche
Tho rounnede sche a pistyl in hyse ere
And bad hym to be glad and haue no fere
Whan þey been comyn to þe court þis knyȝt
Seyde þat he hadde holde his day þat he hyȝt
And redy was his answere as he sayde
fful manye a nobele wyf and manye a mayde
And manye a wedewe for þat þey ben wyse
The queen hire self syttynge as a iustyse
  
Assembelede been his answerys for to here
And aftyrward þis knyȝt was bode to pere
To euery wyȝt was comaundede silence
And þat þe knyȝt schulde telle in audyence
What thyng þat wordely women louyn best
The knyȝt stod not stille as a beest
But to his questioun anon answerde
With manly voys þat al þe court it herde
Myn lige lady generally quod he
Wemen desyryn to han souereynte
As wel ouyr hire husbondis as ouer hire hove
And for to been in maystrye hem aboue
This is þe moste desyr thow ȝe me kylle
Doth as ȝow leste I am al at ȝoure wille
In al þe court ne was þere wif ne mayde
Ne wedewe contraryede þat he sayde
But seydyn þat he was worthi to han his lyf
And with that word vp sterte þe olde wyf
Whiche þat þe knyȝt saw syttynge on þe grene  
Mercy quod sche myn souereyn lady quene
Er þat ȝoure court departe doth me ryght
I taughte this answere to þe knyth
ffor which he plyȝte me his trouthe þere
The fyrste thyng þat I wolde hym requere
He wolde it do ȝif it lay in his myȝt
Byfore þe court þanne preye I þe syre knyȝt
Quod sche þat þou me take on to þyn wyf
ffor weel þou wist þat I haue kept þyn lyf
ȝif I seye fals say nay vpon þy fey
This knyȝt answerde allas and weyleawey
I wot ryȝt wel þat swich was myn beheste
ffor goddys loue as ches a newe requeste
Tak al myn good and lat myn body goo
Nay þanne quod sche I be schrewe vs boþe too
ffor þow I be foul old and pore
I nolde for al þe metal ne for ore
  
That vndyr þe erþe is graue or lyth aboue
But ȝif þyn wyf I were and ek þyn loue
Myn loue quod he nay myn dampnacyoun
Allas þat ony of myn nacyoun 
Schulde euere so foule disparagit be
But al for nouȝt þanne is þis quod sche
Constreynede was he nedys he muste hyre wedde
And takyth his olde wif and goth to bedde
Now wil some men seye parauenture
That for myn neclygens I do no cure
To telle ȝow þe ioye and also tharray
That at þat ilke feste was þat day
To whiche thyng sothely I answere schal
And seye þere was no Ioye ne feste at al
There was but heuynesse and meche sorwe
ffor priuyly he wedde hire in þe morwe
And al day aftyr hydde hym as an houle
So 1wo was1 hym his wyf lokede so foule
Gret was þe wo þe knyȝt hadde in his thouȝt
Whan he was wyth his wyf in bedde Ibrouȝt
He walwith and he turnyth too and fro  
This olde wif lay smylynge euere mo
And seyde o dere husbende benedicite
ffaryth euery knyȝt with his wyf as ȝe
Is þis þe lawe of kyng arthures hous
Is euery knyȝt of his þus daungerous
I am ȝoure owene loue and ȝoure wyf
I am sche þat sauede hath ȝoure lyf
And sertis I dede ȝow neuere vnryȝt
Whi fare ȝe þus with me þe ferste nyȝt
ȝe fare lyk a man þat hadde lost his wit
What is myn gilt for godis loue telle me it
And it schal been amendit ȝif þat I may
Amendit quod this knyȝt allas nay nay
It wele not been amendit neuere mo
Thow art so loothly old and so pore also
  
And þerto comyn of so low a kynde
That lytyl wondir ist þow I walwe and wynde
So wolde god myn herte wolde breste
Is þis quod sche þe cause of ȝoure onreste
ȝa serteynly quod he no wondir is
Now sere quod sche I coude amende al þis
ȝif þat me lyste er it were dayis thre
So wel myȝte ȝe bere ȝow to me
But for ȝe speke of swich gentillesse
As is dessendit out of olde richesse
That þerfore schul ȝe ben holdyn gentil men
Swich arrogaunce is not worth an hen
Loke ho þat is most verteuous alwey
Pryue and apert and most entendyth ay
To do þe gentyl dedys þat he can
Take hym for þe gretteste gentil man
Cryst wele we cleyme of hym oure gentylesse
Noght of oure elderys for oure olde rychesse
ffor þow þey ȝeue vs al here erytage
ffor which we cleymyn to been of high parage
ȝit may þey not byquethe for no thyng
To noon of vs here verteuous lyuyng
That made hem gentylmen Icallede be  
And bad vs foldyn hem in swich degre
Weel can þe wise poete of florence
That hyȝt dant declare þis centence
Lo in swych a manere rym is dantes tale
fful selde vp rysith by hyse braunchis smale
Prowesse of man for god of his prowesse
Wele þat we cleyme of hym oure gentillesse
ffor of oure eldere we may no thyng cleyme
But temperel thyng þat man may hurte and mayme
Ek euery wyȝt wot þis as wel as I
ȝif gentillesse were plantid naturelly
Vp to a certeyn lennage doun be lyne
Preue nor apert þanne wolde þey neuere fyne
  
To don of gentillesse þe offys
They myȝte don no vilenye nor vice
Tak fyr and bere in þe derkeste hous
Betwyxe this and þe mount of Cankerous
And let men schette þe dore and go þenne
ȝit wil þe fyr lye as fyr and brenne
As twenty thousent men myȝte it byholde
His offise naturel ay wel it holde
Vp peril of myn lyf tyl þat it deye
Here may ȝe wel sen how þat genterye
Is not annexed to possescioun
Sithe folk ne don here operacioun
Alwey as doth the fyr in hise kynde
ffor I wot men may ful ofte fynde
A lordis sone do schame and vilanye
And he þat wele haue prys of his genterye
ffor he was bore of a gentyl hous
And hadde hise olderis nobele and vertuous
And nyle hym self don non gentyle dedis
Ne folwe his gentyle auncetere þat deed is
He nys not gentyl be he duk or el
ffor violens synful dedys make eke a cherl
ffor gentillesse nys but renomee
Of thynne auncestris for here hygh bounte
Whiche is a strong thyng to thyn persone  
The gentillesse comyth from god alone
Thanne comyth oure verray gentillesse of grace
It was no thyng bequethe vs with oure place
Thynkith how nobele as seyth valerius
Was that ilke tullius hostilius
That out of pouert ros to gret noblesse
Redyth senec and redith eek boece
Ther schul ȝe se expres þat no dred is
That he is gentyl that doth gentyl dedis
And þerfore leue husbonde I thus conclude
Al were it þat myne auncestris were reude
  
ȝit may þe hye god and so hope I
Graunte me grace to leue verteuosly
Thanne am I gentyl whan þat I begynne
To leuyn verteuously and leuyn synne
And þere as ȝe of pouert me repreue
The hye god of whom ȝe me repreue
In wilful pouert ches to lede his lyf
And certys euery man mayde or wyf
May vndyrstondyn Ihesus heuene kyng
Ne wolde not chese an vicious leuyng
Glad pouert is an oneste thyng certeyn
This wele Senek and oþere clerkys seyn
Ho so hym halt payed of his pouerte
I holde hym ryche hadde he but a sherte
He þat coueytyth is a pore wight
ffor he wolde han þat is not in his myȝt
But he þat nought haht ne coueythit to haue
Is riche althow men holde hym but a knaue
Veray pouert it syngith properly
Iuenal seyth of pouerte meryly
The poure man whan he goth by the weye
Byfore þe thewis he may synge and pleye
Pouerte is hateful good as I gesse
A ful gret bryngere out of besinesse
A gret amendere ek of sapience
To hem þat takyth it in pacience
Pouerte is this althow it seme alenge  
Possessioun þat no man wele calenge
Pouerte ful ofte whan a man is lowe
Makyth his god and hym self to knowe
Pouerte a spectakele is as thynkyth me
Thorw whech he may his veray frend Ise
And þerfore syre syn þat I ȝow not greue
Of myn pouerte no more ȝe me repreue
Now syre of olde ȝe repreue me
And sertis syde thogh non autoryte
  
Were in no bok the gentylys of honour
Seyn þat men schuld an old wyȝt don fauour
And clepyn hym fadyr of ȝoure gentilesse
And auctouris schal I fyndyn as I gesse
Now þere ȝe seyn I am foul and old
Thanne drede ȝow not to ben a coukewold
ffylthe and elde alsomote I the
Ben gret wardaynys vpon chastite
But natheles sythe I knowe ȝoure delyt
I schal fulfylle ȝoure wordely apetyt
Chese now quod sche on of þese thyngis tweye
To haue me foul and old tyl þat I deye
And be to ȝow a trewe vmble wyf
And neuere ȝow displese in al myn lyf
Or ellis ȝe wele haue me ȝyng and fayr
And take þe auenture of the repayr
That schal be to ȝoure hous be cause of me
Or in sum oþer place may wel be
Now cheseth ȝoure selue wheþer þat ȝow likyth
This knyȝt auyseth hym and sore sykyth
But at þe laste he seyde in þis manere
Myn lady and myn loue and myn wyf so dere
I putte me in ȝoure wise gouernaunce
Cheseth ȝoure self whiche may be most plesaunce
And most honour to ȝow and me also
I do no fors wheþer of the too
ffor as ȝow lykyth it suffyseth me
Thanne haue I gete þe maysterye quod sche
Syn I may chese and gouerne as me leste  
ȝa sertys wif quod he I helde it for þe beste
Kis me quod sche we be no lengere wrothe
ffor be myn trouthe I wele be to ȝow bothe
That is to seyne bothe fayr and good
I preye to god I mote sterwe wod
But I to ȝow be al so good and trewe
As euere was wyf syn þat þe world was newe
  
And but I be to morwe as fayr to sene
As eny lady Emperesse or quene
That euere was betwixse þe Est and þe west
Doth with myn lyf and doth ryȝt as ȝow lest
Cast vp þe curtyn and loke how þat it is
And whan þat þe knyght saw verrayly al þis
That sche so fayr was and so ȝyng þerto
ffor ioye he hente hyre in hise armys too
His herte bathit in a bath of blys
A thousent sythe a rowe he gan hire kys
And sche obeyede hym in euery thyng
That myȝte do hym plesaunce or lykyng
And þus þey lyue vnto here lyuys ende
In parfyt Ioye and Ihesu crist vs synde
Husbondis meke ȝinge and frosche in bedde
And grace to ouer byde hem þat we wedde
And ek I preye Ihesu schorte here lyuys
That wele not been gouernyd by here wyuys
And olde and angery nygardys of dispence
God sende hem sone verray pestelence

he made alweie a maner louryng chere 
vpon the Sompnour but yet for honeste 
No vilenous worde as yet spak he 
But at the laste he seide vnto the wif 
Dame gode god yeue you right good lif 
Ye han touched here also mote I the 
In scole mater gret difficulte 
Ye han seide mochell thyng right well I seie   
But dame here as we riden bi the weie 
Vs nedith not to speken but of game 
And late auctorites go a goddis name 
To prechyng and to scole eke of clergie 
But if it like vnto this companye 
I will you of a somnour telle a game 
Parde ye may well knowe be the name 
That of no somnour may no gode be saide 
I praye that non of you be euyll apaide 
A Somnour is a romere vp and doun 
With maundementis of ffornycacioun 
And is bete at euery townes ende 
Our oost tho spak a sir ye schulde ben hende 
And curteis as man of your estate 
In companye we woll no debate 
Telleth your tale and lateth the Somnour be 
Nay quod the Somnour late hym saie to me
What so hym list whan it cometh to my lot 
Bi god I schall hym quyte euery grot 
I schall hym telle whiche a gret honour 
It is to be a flateryng lymytour 
And eek of full manye another cryme 
Whiche nedith not rehersen at this tyme 
And his office I schall hym telle ywis 
Our hoste answerid pees no more of this 
And aftirwarde he seide vnto the ffrere 
Tell forth your tale my leue maister dere 
WHilom ther was dwellyng in my contre 
An Erchedekene a man of hye degre 
That boldely dide execucioun 
In ponyschyng of ffornycacioun 
Of wicchecrafte and eek of baudrie 
Of diffamacioun and avoutrie 
Of chirche reeues and of testamentis 
Of contractis and of lak of sacramentis 
Of vsure and Symonye also 
But certis lecchours dide he most wo 
Thei schulden syngen if thei were hent 
And smale tithers weren foule schent 
Yf ony persone wolde vpon hem pleyne 
Ther myght asterte hym no pecunyall peyne 
ffor smale tithes and eek smale offerynge 
he made the peple spitously to synge 
ffor or the Bischop caughte hem with his hooke 
Thei weren in the Erchedekenes booke 
And then had he thorow his Iurdiccion   
Power to doon on hem correccion 
he had a Sompnour redy to his honde 
A slier boie was non in Engelonde 
ffor subtily he hadde hise expyayle  
That tauȝte hym where hym myȝte avayle
He coude spare of lechourys on or two
To techyn hym to foure and twenty mo
ffor þow þis somenour wood were as an hare
To telle his harloterye I wele not spare
  
ffor we ben out of his coreccioun
They han of vs no Iurediccioun
Ne neuere ne schuln of alle here lyuys
Petyr so been wemen at þe styuys
Quod þe somenour Iput out of oure cure
Pees with myschaunce and with mysauenture
Thus seyde oure ost and lat hym telle his tale
Now tellith forth þow þat þe somenour gale
Ne sparyth not myn owene maystyr dere
This false thef þis somenour quod þe frere
Hadde alwey baudys redy to his hond
As ony hauk to lure in ingelond
That tolde hym al þe secre þat þey knewe
ffor hire aqueyntauns was not comyn of newe
They were hise apprououris pryuyly
He tok hym self a profyt þerby
His maystyr knew not alwey what he wan
Withoutyn maundement a lewede man
He coude somounne vp peyne of crystis curs
And þey were ful glad to fille his purs
And made hym noble festis at þe nale
And ryȝt as Iudas hadde purse smale
And was a thef ryȝt swich a thef was he
Hise mayster hadde but half his duete
He was ȝif I schal ȝeuyn hym hise lawede
A thef and ek a somenour and a baude
He hadde ek wenchis at his retenew
That wheþer syre Robert oþer syre Hewe
Or Iakke or Raf or who so þat it were
That lay by hem þey tolde it in hise ere
Thus was þe wenche and he at on assent
And he wolde feche a feynede maundement
And somoune hem to chapitere boþe two  
And pile þe man and lete þe wenche go
Thanne wolde he sey frend I schal for thyn sake
Don stryke þe out of oure letteris blake
  
The thar no more as in þis cas trauayle
I am thyn frend þere I þe may avayle
Certeyn he knew of bryberyis mo
Than possible is to telle in ȝeris two
ffor in þis world nys doge for þe bowe
Than kan an hurt der from an hol knowe
Bet þan þe somenour knew a sly lechour
Or auoutir or a paramour
And for þat was þe freut of al his rente
Therfore he sette on it al hyse entente
And so befel þat onys on a day
This somenour euere waytynge on hyse pray
Wente for to somounne a wedewe an old rybibe
ffeynynge a cause for he wolde brybe
And happede he saw byfore hym ryde
A gay ȝeman vndir a forest syde
A bowe he bar and arwis bryȝte and kene
He hadde upon a courtepy of grene
An hat vpon his hed with frengis blake
Syre quod þe somenour wel atake
Wolcome quod he and euery good felawe
Wheþer rydistow vndyr þis grene wode schawe
Seyde þis ȝeman wilt þou fer to day
This somenour answerde and seyde nay
Here faste by is myn entente
To rydyn and to reysyn vp a rente
That longith on to myn lordis duete
Art þou þanne a baylyf  ye quod he
He durste not for veray fylthe and schame
Seye he was a somenour for þe name
Depardeus quod þis ȝeman leue broþer
Thou art a balyf and I am anoþer
I am onknowyn as in þis cuntre
Of thyn aqueyntauns I wolde preye þe
And ek of brotherhode ȝif that ȝow leste  
I haue gold and siluyr in myn cheste
  
ȝif þat ȝe happyn to comyn in oure schyre
Al schal be ryȝt as ȝe wele desyre
Graunt mercy quod þis somenour be myn fey
Eueryche in oþeres hand his trouthe leyth
ffor to ben swore breþeryn tyl þey deye
In daliaunce þey ryde forth and pleye
This somenour þat was so ful of Iangelys
As ful of venym ben þese variangelys
And euere enquyrynge vpon euery thyng
Brothir quod he where is ȝoure dwellyng
Anoþer day ȝif þat I schulde ȝow seche
This ȝeman hym answerede in softe speche
Broþer quod he fer in þe north cuntre
Where as I hope sumtyme I schal þe se
Er we departe I schal þe so wel wische
That of myn hous ne shalt þou neuere mysse
Now broþer quod þe somenour I ȝow preye
Teche me whils þat ȝe ryde by þe weye
Syn þat ȝe be a balyf as am I
Sum subtilete and telle me feythfully
In myn offys how I may most wynne
And sparyth not for concience ne for synne
But as myn broþer telle me how do ȝe
Now by myn trouthe broþer dere seyde he
As I schal telle þe a feythful tale
Mynne wagis been ful streyte and ful smale
Myn lord is hard to me and daungerous
And myn offys is ful laberous
And þerfore by extorciounnys I leue
ffor sothe I take al þat men wele me ȝeue
Algate by sleyȝte or by violence
ffrom ȝer to ȝer I wynne al myn dispence
I can no betere telle feythfully
Now sertis quod þis somenour so fare I
I spare not to take god it wot
But ȝif it be to heuy or to hoot
  
What I may gete in conseyl pryuyly  
No manere concience haue I
Nere myn extorcioun I myȝte not lyue
Ne of sweche Iapis I wele not be schreue
Stomak ne concience knowe I non
I schrewe þese schryft faderys euerychon
Wel be we met by god and by seynt Iame
But leue broþer telle me þanne þyn name
Quod this somenour and in þis mene while
This ȝeman gan a lytyl for to smyle
Broþer quod he wilt þou þat I þe telle
I am a fend myn dwellyng is in helle
And here I ryde aboute myn purchasyng
To wete where men wolde ȝeue me ony thyng
Myn purchas is þe effect of al myn rente
Loke how þou rydist for þe same entente
To wynne good þou rekist neuere how
Ryght so fare I for ryde wolde I now
Vnto þe worldis ende for a preye
A quod þe somenour benediste what seye
I wende ȝe were a ȝeman trewely
ȝe haue a manys schap as wel as I
Hue ȝe a figure þanne determynat
In helle þere ȝe ben in ȝoure estat
Nay serteyn quod he þere haue we non
But whan vs lykyth þanne can we takyn on
Or ell make ȝow seme þat we been schape
Sumtyme lyk a man or lyk an ape
Or lyk an aungel can I ryde or go
It is no wondyr thyng thow it be so
A lousy iogelour can deseyue þe
And parde ȝit can I more craft þan he
Whi quod þe somenour ride ȝe þanne or gon
In sundery schap and not alwey in on
ffor we quod he wele vs swich formys make
As most able is oure prey for to take
  
What makyth ȝow to haue al þis labour
fful manye a cause leue sire Somenour
Seyde þis fend but alle thynge hath tyme  
The day is schort  and it is passede pryme
And ȝit ne wan I no thyng on this day
I wele entende to wynnyng ȝif I may
And noght entende oure wordis to declare
ffor broþer myn thyn wit is al to bare
To vndyrstonde al thow I tolde hem the
But for þou axsyst why laboure we
ffor sumtyme we ben goddys instrumentis
And meeuy for to don hise comaundementis
Whan þat hym lyste vpon hyse creaturys
In dyuerse art and in dyuerse figurys
Withoutyn hym we haue no myȝt certeyn
ȝif þat him liste stande þere ageyn
And sumtyme at oure preyere han we leue
Only þe body but not þe soule to greue

And some tyme haue we myȝt of bothe two  
This is to seyne of soule and body ek
And sumtyme be we sufferede for to sek
Vpon a man and don his soule onreste
Noght his body and al is for þe beste
Whan he withstandith oure temptacioun
It is þe cause of his sauacioun
Al be it þat it was not oure entente
He schulde be saf but þat we wolde hym hente
And sumtyme be we seruauntys vnto man
As to þe Erchebischop seynt Dunstan
And to þe apostell ek seruauaunt was I
ȝit telle me quod þe sumnour feythfully
Make ȝe ȝow newe bodyis þus alwey
Of elementis  þe fend answerde nay
Sumtyme we feyne and sumtyme we areyse
With deede bodyis in ful sundery wyse
  
And speke as renable and fayre and wel
As to þe Phitonyssa dede Samuel
And ȝit wele some men seyn it was nat
I do no fors of ȝoure dyuynyte
But o thyng warne I þe I wele not iape
Thow wolt algatis wete how we ben schape
Thow schalt here aftyward myn broþer dere  
Come  where þe nedyth not of me to lere
ffor þou schat by thyn owene experyence
Cunne in a chayer þanne rede þis sentence
Bet þan virgilie whilis he w on lyue
Or daunt also whils he was on lyue
ffor I wele holde cumpanye with þe
Til it be so þat þou forsake me
Nay quod þe somenour þat schal neuere betyde
I am a ȝeman knowyn is ful wyde
Myn trouthe wele I holde 
ffor þouȝe þou were þe Deuell Sathanas
My trouþe wolle I holde  
As I am sworn and eche of vs tyl oþer
ffor to be trewe broþer in þis cas
And boþe we gon aboute oure purchas
Take þou þyn part of þat men wele þe ȝeue
And I schal myn þus may we boþe leue
And ȝif þat ony of vs haue more þan oþer
Let hym be trowe and parte it with his broþer
I graunte quod þe deuyl be myn fey
And with þat word þey ryde forth here wey
And ryȝt at þe enterynge at þe tounnys ende
To which þis somenour schop hym for to wende
The saw a carte þat chargede was with hey
Which þat a Cartere drof ferth in þe wey
Dep was þe weye for which þis carte stod
The cartere smot and cryede as he were wood
Hayt sket hayt lyarad hat brok atonys
The fend quod he ȝow feche body and bonys
  
As ferforth as euere were ȝe folyd
So meche woo as I haue with ȝow tholyd
The deuyl haue al boþe hors and carte and hey
The somenour seyde here schul we haue a pley
And ner þe frere he drow as nouȝt ne were
fful priuyly and rounnede in his ere
Herke myn broþer herke be thyn feith
Heryst þou nought how þe cartere seyth
Hende it anon for he hath ȝouen it þe
Boþe hey and carte and ek his capillis thre
Nay quod þe deuyl neuere a del  
It is not his entente troste wel
Axe hym thyn self ȝif þou not trostiste me
Or ellis stynte awhile and þou schat se
This cartere thakkyth hise hors vpon þe croupe
And þey begunne to drawe and to stoupe
Hayt now quod he now Ihesu cryst ȝow blysse
And al hise hondwerk boþe more and lesse
That was wel twyȝt myn owene lyard boy
I preye god saue þe body and seynt loy
Now is myn carte out of the slow parde
Lo broþer quod þe fend what tolde I the
Heere may ȝe seen myn owene dere broþer
The cherl spak on thyng and mente anoþer
Lat vs gon forth aboutyn oure viage
Here wynne I no good vpon caryage
Whan þat þey comyn sumwhat out of tounne
This somenour to his broþer gan to rounne
Broþer quod he here wonyth an old rebekke
That hadde almost as lef to lese his nekke
As for to ȝeue a peny of hire good
I wele haue twelue penys thow sche be wood
Or I wele somounne hyre to oure offys
And ȝit god wot can I no vys
But for þou canyst not as in þis cuntre
Wynne thyn cost take here ensaumple at me
  
This somenour clepith at þe wedewis gate
Come out quod he þou olde verye crate
I trowe þou hast sum frere or prest with the
Ho clepith þere seyde þis widew benedicice
God saue ȝow syre what is ȝoure swete wille
I haue quod he of somounnys a bille
Vp peyne of cursynge loke þat þou be
To morwe byfore þe Erchedekenys kne
To answere to þe court of serteyn thyngis
Now lord quod sche Ihesu kyng of kyngis
So wysely helpe me as I ne may
I haue be sek and þat ful manye a day
I may not goon quod sche so fer ne ryde  
But I be ded so prykyth it in myn syde
May I not axe a libel syre somenour
And answere þere by myn procatour
To swich thyng as men wele oposyn me
ȝis quod this somenour pay anon lat se
Twelue penys lat se and I wele þe aquyte
I schal no profyit haue þerby but lyte
Myn maystir hath the profit and not I
Come of and let me rydyn hastely
ȝeue me twelve penys I may no lengere lette
Twelue penys quod sche now lady seynte marye
So wysely helpe me out of care and synne
This wyde world þow þat I schulde wynne
Ne haue I not twelue penys withinne myn holld
ȝe knowe wel þat I am pore and old
Kythe ȝoure almesse on me pore wreche
Nay þanne quod he þe fend me feche
ȝif I þe excuse thw þow schuldist be spylt
Allas quod sche god wot I haue no gilt
Pay me quod he or be swete seynt anne
As I wele bere awey þyn newe panne
ffor dette whiche þou owist me of old
Whan þat þou haddist þyn husbonde coukewold
  
I payede at hom for þyn coreccioun
Thow lyxt quod sche be myn sauacyoun
Ne was I neuere er no wedewe ne wyf
Somounede on to ȝoure court in al myn lyf
Ne neuere I nas but of myn body trewe
Vnto þe deuyl blak and row of hewe
ȝeue I thyn body and myn panne also
And whan þe deuyl herde hire curse so
Vpon hire kneis sche seyde on þis manere
Now mabelyn myn owene modir dere
Is þis ȝoure wille in ernest þat ȝe seye
The deuyl quod sche so feche hym er he deye
And panne and al but he wele hym repente
Nay olde stot þat is not myn entente

ffor eny þenge þat I haue hade of þe
I wolde I hade þi smok and euery clothe
Nowe Broþer quod þe Deuyll be not wrothe
Thy body and þis panne ys myne by riȝt
Thou shalte with me to helle · ȝit to nyȝt
þere þou shalt knowe of oure pryuete
More þan a Maystre of Diuinite
And with þat worde þe foule fende hym hent
Body and soule with þe fende went
Where þat Somonours haue hir herytage
And god þat made aftyr hys Image
Mankynde saue and gyde vs alle and somme
And leue þis Somonour gode man bycome
Lordynges I coude a tolde you quod þe frere  
Hade I hade leyser of thys Somnour here
After þe Tyxt Cryst poule and Iohn 
And of other doctours many on 
Suche peynes þat youre hertes may agryse 
Also by hyt þat no þenge may deuyse 
Thou þat I myȝt a þousand wynter telle 
The peyne of þilke Cursed house of helle 
  
But for to kepe vs fro þat cursed place
Wakethe and preithe Ihesu for his grace
To kepe vs  fro þe Temptour Sathanas
herken þis worde be ware in þis caas
The lyonn sit in his wayt alway
To sle þe Innocent yf þat he may
Disposethe ay youre hertes to withstonde
þe fende þat you wolde make þrall and bonde
he may not tempten you ouere your myȝt
And Cryst woll be youre Champioun and your knyȝt
And preythe þat þis Sompnour hym repent
Of hys mysdede or þe fende hym hent
THis Somnour in his stirop hye stood 
Vpon this ffrere his herte was so wood 
That like an Aspen leef he quoke for yre 
Lordyngis quod he but oo thyng I desire 
I you beseke that of your curtesie 
Sethyns ye han herd this fals ffrere lye 
As suffreth me I maye a tale telle   
This ffrere bosteth that he knoweth helle 
And god woot that it is litell wondir
ffreres and fendes ben but litell a sondir
ffor parde ye han ofte tyme herd telle 
how that a ffrere rauysched was in to helle 
In spirit onys by a visioun 
And as an angell lad hym vp and doun 
To schewyn hym the peynes that ther were 
In all the place sawe he not a ffrere 
Of other folke he sawe ynow in woo 
Vnto this angell spake the ffrere tho 
Now sir quod he han ffreres suche grace 
That non of hem schall come to this place 
Yes quod this angell manye a mylioun 
And vnto Sathanas he lad hym adoun 
And now hath Sathanas saith he a taile 
Bradder then of the Carik is the saile 
Holde vp thyn taile Sathanas quod he 
Schewe forth thyne ers and lete the ffrere se 
Where is the neste of ffreres in this place 
And er that half a forlong wey of space 
  
Right so as Bees swermen out of an hyue 
Out of the deuylles ers thei gon dryue 
xxti thousande ffreris on a route 
And thorowout helle swarmed all aboute 
And camen ayen as fast as thei may gone 
And in his ers thei crepedyn euerichone 
He clapt his tale ayen and laye still 
This ffrere when he lokid had his fill 
Vpon this tormentis of this sory place 
his spirit god restorid of his grace 
Vnto his bodye ayen and he awoke 
But natheles for fere yet he quoke 
So was the deuelis ars ay in his mynde 
That is his heritage of verrey kynde 
God saue you alle saue this cursid ffrere 
Mi Prolog woll I ende in this manere 
LOrdyngis ther is in york schire as I gesse
A merschy contre called holdernesse
In whiche ther wente a lymytour aboute
To preche and eek to begge it is no doute
And so bifell that on a daye this ffrere
had preched at chirche in this manere
And specially abouyn euery thyng
Excited he the peple in his prechyng
To trentalis and to yeue for goddis sake  
Wherwith men myghte holi housis make
Ther as deuyne seruyse is honoured
Nought ther as it is wasted and deuoured
Ne there it nedith not for to be yeue
As to possessioners that may ellis lyue
Thanked be god in wele and habundaunce
Trentales seide he delyuerith fro penaunce
Here frendes soules as well olde as yong
Yef that thei ben hastely song
Nought for to holde a preest ioly and gay
he syngeth not but oo messe in a day
Delyuerith out a man quod he the soulis
ffull hard it is with fleschehoke or with oulis
Now spede you hastely for cristes sake
To kepe you fro peynes of fendis blake
And whan the ffrere had seide alle his entente
With Qui cum patre forth he wente
When folke in chirche had yeue hym what hem lest
he wente his way no lenger wolde he rest
  
With scrippe and tipped staf tucked full hye
In euery hous he gan to pore and prye
And beggeth mele or chese or ellis corn
his felalawe had a staf tipped with horn
A peire of tablis of yuory
And a poyntell polched fetisly
And wrot alweye the names there he stood
Of alle folke that yaf hym any good
Ascaunce as he wolde for hem preie
Yeue vs a buschell whete malt or reie
A godis kechil or a trip of chese  
Or ellis what ȝow lyste we may not chese
A godis halpeny or a masse pany
Or ȝeue vs of ȝoure braun ȝif ȝe han any
A dagoun of ȝoure blanket leue dame
Oure sistyr dere lo here I wryte ȝoure name
Bacoun or bef or swich þyng as ȝe fynde
A sturdy harlot wente hem ay byhynde
That was here ostys man and bar a sak
And what men ȝoue hem leyde it on his bak
And whan he was out at þe dore anon
He planede awey þe namys euerychon
That he before hadde wrytyn in hyse tablis
He servede hem with nyflys and wyth fablys
Nay þere þou lext þou somenour quod þe frere
Pes quod oure ost for cristis modyr dere
Telle forth ȝoure tale and spare it not at al
So thryue I quod the somenour so I schal
So longe he wente hous be hous tyl he
Cam to an hous þere he was wone to be
Refresched more þan in an hunderede placis
Sek lay þe goode man whos þe place is
Bedrede vpon a couche lowe he lay
Deus hic quod he O tomays frend good day
Seyde þis frere curteysly and softe
Thomas quod he god ȝelde ȝow ful ofte
  
Haue I vpon þis benche fare ful wel
Here haue I ete ful manye a murye mel
And fro þe bench he drof awoy þe cat
And leyde adoun his potente and his hat
And ek his scryppe and sette hym softe adoun
His felawe was go walkede in þe toun
fforth with his knawe vnto þat ostelrye
Where as he schop hym þe ilke nyȝt to lye
O dere maystir quod þis syke man
How haue ȝe fare sythe þat March began
I saw ȝow not þis fourtenyȝt or more
God wot quod he laboured haue I ful sore
And spcially for thyn saluacioun  
Haue I seyd manye a precious orisoun
And for oure oþere frendis god hem blysse
I haue to day been at ȝoure cherche at messe
And seyd a sarmoun aftyr myn symple wit
Nat al aftyr þe text of holy wret
ffor it is hard to ȝow as I suppose
And þerfore wele I telle ȝow al þe glose
Glosyng is a glorious thyng serteyn
ffor lettere sleth as we clerkis seyn
There haue I tauȝt hem to be charytable
And spende here good þere it is resonable
And þere I saw oure dame a where is sche
Ȝond in þe ȝerd I trowe þat sche be
Seyde þis man and sche wele come anon
Ey maystir wolcome be ȝe by seynt Iohn
Seyde þis wif how fare ȝe hertely
This frere arysith vp ful curteysly
And hire enbraseth in hise armys narwe
And kysseth hire swete  and chirketh as a sparwe
With his lippis dame quod he ryȝt wel
As he þat is ȝoure seruaunt euerydel
Thankede be god þat ȝow ȝaf soule and lyf
ȝit saw I not þis day so fayr a wyf
  
In al þe cherche god so saue me
ȝa god amende þe fautis sere quod sche
Algatis wolcome ȝe by myn fey
Graunt merci dame þis haue I founde alwey
But of ȝoure grete goodnesse by ȝoure leue
I wolde preye ȝow þat ȝe nat ȝow greve
I wele with Thomas speke a lytyl throwe
These curatis been ful neglygent and slowe
To grope tenderely a concience
In schrifte in prechynge is myn diligence
And stodie in peteris wordis and in Poulis
I walke to fyche cristene menys soulys
To ȝilde Ihesu crist  hise propere rente
To sprede his word is set al myn entente
Now by ȝoure leue o deere maystyr quod sche  
Schidith hym wel for seynte trynyte
He is as angery as a pissemyre
Thow that he haue al þat he can desyre
Thow I hym wrye a nyȝt and make hym warm
And ouer hym leye myn leg oþer myn arm
He gronyth lik oure bor lyth in oure sty
Oþer disport ryȝt non of hym haue I
I may not plese hym in no manere cas
O Thomas Ie vous dy Thomas Thomas
This makyth þe feend þis muste ben amendit
Ire is a thyng þat highe god defendit
And þerof wele I speke a word or two
Now maystir quod þe wyf er þan I go
What wele ȝe dyne I wele go þere aboute
Now dame quod he Ie vous dy sanz doute
Haue I nat of a capoun but þe lyuere
And of ȝoure softe bred but a scheuere
And aftyr þat a rostede pigis hed
But þat I nolde no beste for me were ded
Thanne hadde I with ȝow homely suffysaunce
I am a man of lytyl sustenaunce
  
Myn spirit hath his fosterynge in þe bible
The bodi is ay so redy and penible
To wake þat myn stomak is distroyed
I prey ȝow dame ȝe be nat anoyed
Thow I so frendely ȝow myn conseyl schewe
By god I nolde nat telle it but a fewe
Now syre quod sche but on word er I go
Myn child is deed withinne these woukis too
Sone aftyr þat ȝe wentyn out of þis toun
His deth saw I be reuelacioun
Seyde þis frere at hom in oure dortour
I dar wel seyn þat er þat half an our
Aftyr his deth I saw hym bore to blysse
In myn auysioun god so me wisse
So dede oure sexteyn and oure fermorer
That han ben trewe frerys fifty ȝer
They may now god be thanked of his lone  
Makyn here Iubyle and walkyn alone
And vp I ros and al oure couent ek
With manye a tere trynkelynge on myn cheke
Withoutyn noyse or claterynge of bellis
Te deum was oure song and no thyng ellis
Saue þat to cryst I seyde an orysoun
Thankynge hym of myn reuelacioun
ffor sere and dame trostith to me wel
Oure orisounys ben more effectuel
And more we sen of secre thyngis
Than burel folk al þow þey were kyngis
We lyue in pouert and in abstinence
And burel folk in rychesse and dispence
In mete and drynk and in here foule delyt
We han þis wordelis lust al in dispit
Laȝar and dyuers leuedyn dyuers lyf
And dyuers gerdoun haddyn þey þerby
Ho so wele preye  hym muste faste and be clene
And fattyn his soule and make his body leene
  
We faryn as seyth þe appostele cloth and fode
Suffyseth vs  þow þey been not ful goode
The clennesse and þe fastynge of vs frerys
Makyth þat cryst  acceptyth oure preyerys
Lo moyses forty dayis and forty nyȝt
ffastid er þat þe hyghe god of myȝt
Spak with hym in þe mount of synay
With emty wombe  fastynge manye a day
Resseyuede he þe lawe þat was wretyn
With godis fyngir and elye wolde wetyn
In Mount oreb er he hadde any speche
With hye god þat is oure lyuys leche
He fastede longe and was in contemplaunce
Aaron þat hadde þe temple in gouernaunce
And ek þe oþere postellis euerychon
Into þe temple whan þey schulde gon
To preye for þe peple and do seruyse
The nolde drynke in no manere wyse
No drynk whiche þat myȝte hem dronke make  
But þere in abstinence preye and wake
Lest þat þey dey dyn tak hede what I seye
But þey ben sobere þat for þe puple preye
War þat I seye no more for it suffyseth
Oure lord Ihesu as holy wryt deuyseth
ȝaf vs ensaumple of fastynge and preyerys
Therefore we mendynauntis we frerys

To charite humblenesse and pacience
To persecucion for rightwisnesse
To wepyng mysericord and clennesse
And therfore maye ye se that our praieres
I speke of vs we mendenauntis we ffreres
Been to þe hye god more acceptable
Than ȝoure is  with ȝoure festis at þe table
ffrom paradys fyrst ȝif I schal nat lye
Was man out chased for his glotenye
  
And chaast was man in paradys serteyn
But herke now thomas what I schal seyn
I ne haue of it no text as I suppose
But I schal fynde it in anoþer glose
That specyally oure swete lord Ihesus
Spak þis be freris whan he seyde þus
Blyssede ben þey þat poore in spiryt been
And so forth al þe gospel may ȝe sen
Wheþer it be lykere oure profescioun
Or hire þat swemyn in possessioun
ffy on hire pompe and on here gletenye
And for here lewedenesse I hem defye
Me thynkyth þey been lyk to Iouynyan
ffat as a whal and walkynge as a swan
Al vinolent as botel in þe spence
Hire preyere is of ful gret reuerence
Whan þey for soulis seyn þe salme of dauith
Lo buf þey seye  cor meum erouctauyth
Ho folwyth cristis gospel and hise fore
But we þat vmble ben and chaste and poore
Werkeris of godis word not audytourys
Therfore ryȝt as an hauk ryȝt at a sourys
Vp spryngith in þe eyre ryȝt so preyerys
Of charytable and chaste besy frerys
Makyn here sours to goddys erys two
Thomas Thomas so mote I ryde or go
And by þe lord þat clepid is seynt Iue  
Nere þou oure broþer schudist þou not thryue
In oure chapitre preye we day and nyȝt
To cryst þat he þe sende hele and myȝt
Thyn body for to wendyn hastyly
God wot þerof nothyng þerof fele I
So helpe me crist as in a fewe ȝerys
I haue spendit vpon dyuers maner frerys
fful manye a pound ȝit fare I neuere þe bet
Certeyn myn good haue I almost beset
  
ffarwel myn good for it is al a go
The frere answerde O thomas dost þou so
What nedyth ȝow dyuers frerys seche
What nedyth hym þat hath a parfit leche
To sechyn oþere lechis in þe toun
Ȝoure inconstaunce is ȝoure confusioun
Holde ȝe þanne me or ellis oure couent
To preye for ȝow ben ensufficient
Thomas þat Iape nys nat worth a myte
Ȝoure malady is for ȝe han to lyte
A ȝif þat couent half a quarter otys
And ȝif þat couent foure and twenty grotis
And ȝif þat frere a peny and lat hym go
Nay nay Thomas It may no thyng be so
What is a ferthyg worth partid on twelve
Lo eche thyng þat is onyd in hym selue
Is more strong þan whan it is toskateryd
Thomas of me þou schalt not ben Iflatered
Thow woldyst han oure labour al for nouȝt
The hie god þat al þis world hath wrouȝt
Seyth þat þe werke man worthy is his hyre
Thomas noght of ȝoure tresore I desyre
As for myn self but þat al oure couent
To preye for ȝow is ay so diligent
And for to bildyn cristis owene chyrche
Thomas ȝif ȝe wele lerne for to werche
Of bildyng vp of cherchis may ȝe fynde
Ȝif it be good in Thomas lyf of ynde
Ȝe lye here ful of anguyssch and of yre  
With wych þe deuyl set ȝoure hette afyre
And chidyn here þis sely innosent
Ȝoure wif þat is so meeke and pacient
And þerfore Thomas trowe me if þe lest
Ne stryue nat with þyn wif as for þe best
And bere þis word awoy now be þyn feyth
Touchynge swich thyng lo as þe wyse seyth
  
Withinne þyn hous ne be þou no lyoun
To þynne subiectis do non oppressioun
Ne make þynne aquentauncis not to fle
And Thomas ȝit eft sonys I charge þe
Bywar from hire þat in þyn bosum slepith
Bywar from þe serpent þat so slyly crepith
Vndyr þe gres and styngith subtyly
Bywar myn sone and herke paciently
That twenty thousent men han lost here lyuys
ffor stryuyng with here lemanys and here wyuys
Now sithe ȝe han so holy meke a wyf
What nedyth ȝow Thomas to makyn stryf
There is I wis no serpent so crewel
Whan man trat on his tayl ne half so fel
As woman is whan sche hath cauȝt an yre
Veniaunce is þanne al þat þey desyre
Ire is a synne on of þe gretteste of synnys
Abomynable vnto þe god of heuene
And to hym self it is distruxcioun
This euery lewede veker or parsoun
Kan seen how yre engenderyth homysyde
Ire is in soth executour of pryde
I coude of Ire sey so meche sorwe
Myn tale schulde laste tyl to morwe
And þerfore preye I god boþe day and nyȝt
An yrous man god sende hym lityl myȝt
It is gret harm and ek greet pete
To sette an yrous man in heigh degre
 Whylom þere was an yrous potestat
As seyth Senek þat durynge his estat
Vpon a day out rydyn knyȝtis too  
And as fortune wolde þat it were so
That on of hem cam hom þat oþer nouȝt
Anon þe knyȝt byfore þe Iuge is brouȝt
That seyde þus þou hast þyn felawe slayn
ffor which I deme þe to þe deth sertayn
  
And to anoþer knyȝt comaundede he
Go lede hym to þe deth I charge þe
And happid as þey wente by þe weye
Toward þe place þere he schulde deye
The knyȝt cam which men wende he hadde be ded
Thanne thouȝte þey it was þe beste red
To leede hem boþe to þe Iuge ageyn
They seyde lord þe knyght ne hath not slayn
His felawe here he stondyth hol aloone
Ȝe schul ben ded anoon so mote I gone
That is to seyne boþe on and too and thre
And to þe ferste knyȝt þus spak he
I dampnede þe þu muste algatis be ded
And þou also muste nedys lese þyn hed
ffor þou art cause whi thyn felawe deyeth
And to þe thredde knyȝt ryȝt þus he seyeth
Thow hast not don þat I comaundede þe
And þus he dede hem slen alle thre
Irous Cambises was ek dronkelewe
And ay delitede hym to ben a schrewe
And so befel a lord of his meyne
That louede verteuos moralite
Seyde on a day betwixe hem ryȝt þus
A lord is lost ȝif he be vicious
And dronkenes is ek a foul record
In any man and namely in a lord
There is ful manye an ye and manye an ere
Awaytynge on a lord and he not where
ffor godys loue drynk more atemperelly
Wyn makyth man to lesyn wrechedely
His mynde and hyse lymys euerychon
The reuers schal þou sen and þat anon
And preve it by thyn owene experyence  
That wyn ne doth to folk non swich offence
There is no wyn bereuyth me myn myȝt
Of hond ne foot ne of myn eye syȝt
  
And for despit he drank mekyl þe more
An hunderede part than he hadde don byfore
And ryȝt anon þis yrous cursede wreche
Leet þis knyȝt sone byfore hym feche
Comaundynge hym he schulde byfore hym stonde
And sodeynly he tok his bowe on honde
And vp þe stryng he pullede to hyse ere
And with an arwe he slow þe child ryȝt þere
Now wheþer haue I sekyr hand or non
Quod he is al myn myȝt and mynde agon
Hath wyn bereuyd me myn eyen syth
What schulde I telle þe answere of þe knyȝt
His sone was slaye þere is no more to seye
Beth war þerfore with lordys how ȝe pleye
Syng placebo and I schal ȝif i can
But ȝif it be vnto a pore man
To a pore man men schulde his vicis telle
But not to a lord þow he schulde go to helle
Lo yrous Cyrus thilke percyen
How he distroyed þe Ryuer of Gyseen
ffor þat an hors of his was drenkt þerinne
Whan þat he wente babylonye to wynne
He made þat þe ryuer was so smal
That wemen myghte wade it oueral
Lo what seyde he þat so wel teche can
Ne be no felawe to an yrous man
Ne wyth no wood man walke by þe weye
Lest þe repente I wele no ferþere seye
Now thomas leue broþer lef thyn yre
Thu schalt me fynde as Iust as is a squre
Hold not þe deuyll knyf ay at þyn herte
Thyn angyr doth þe al to sore smerte
But schewe to me al thyn confescioun
Nay quod þe syke man by seynt symoun
I haue be schryue this day at myn curat  
I haue hym told al holy myn estat
  
Nedith it no more to speke of it seyth he
But ȝif me lyste of myn humylite
Ȝif me of ȝore gold to make oure cloystere
Quod he for manye a muskele and manye an oystere
Whan oþere men han ben ful weel at eyse
Hath ben oure fode oure Cloystere for to reyse
And ȝit god wot oneþe þe fondement
Parformed is ne of oure pauuement
Nis not a tyl ȝit withinne oure wonys
By god we owyn fourty pound for stonys
Now help tomays for hym þat harwede helle
Or ellis muste we oure bokys selle
And ȝif ȝow lakke oure predicacioun
Thanne goth þe world al to distruccioun
ffor ho so from þis world wolde vs bereue
So god me saue thomas be ȝoure leue
He wolde bereue out of þis world þe sunne
ffor who can teche and werke as we cunne
And þat is not of lytyme quod he
But sithe þat elye was or elyse
Han frerys ben þat fynde I of record
In charyte thankede be oure lord
Now Thomas help for seynte charyte
And doun anon he sette hym on his kne
This syke man wex ny wood for yre
He wolde þat þe frere hadde bee afyre
With his false dissymylacioun
Swych thyng as is in myn possessioun
Quod he may I ȝeuyn and non oþer
Ȝe sey me þis how þat I am ȝoure broþer
Ȝa certis quod þe frere trostyth wel
I tok oure dame oure lettere with oure sel
Now wel quod he and sumwhat schal I ȝeue
On to ȝoure holy couent whil I leue
And in þyn hand þou schalt it hald anon
On þis condicioun and oþere non
  
That þou departe it so my derere broþer  
That euery frere haue as meche as oþer
This schalt þou swere on þyn professioun
Withoute fraude or cauelacyoun
I swere it quod þe frere vpon myn feith
And þerwithal his hand in his he leith
Lo here myn feyth in me schal ben no lak
Now put þanne þyn hand doun by myn bak
Seyde þis man and grope wel byhynde
Benethe myn buttok þere schat þu fynde
A thyng þat I haue hid in pryuyte
A thoute þis frere þat schal gon with me
And doun his hand he lauchith to þe clyfte
In hope for to fynde þere a ȝifte
And whan þis syke man felte þis frere
Aboute his tewel grope þere and here
Amyd his hand he let þe frere a fart
There nys no capil drawynge in a cart
That myȝt a lete a fart of swych a soun
The frere vpstirte as doth a wood lyoun
A false cherl he seyde for godys bonys
This hast þou for dispit don for þe nonys
þow shalt abeye þis fart ȝif þat I may
His meyne þat herdyn þis afray
Come lepynge in and cachede out þe frere
And forth he goth with a ful angery chere
And fette hese felawe þere as hadde his stor
Ho lokede as it were a wylde boor
He grynt with his teth so was he wroth
A sturdy pas doun to þe court he goth
Where as þere wonede a man of greet honour
To whom þat he was alwey confessour
This worthi man was lord of þat village
This frere cam as he were in a rage
Where as þis lord sit etynge at his bord
Oneþe myȝte þe frere speke a word
  
Tyl at þe laste he seyde god ȝow se
This lord gan to loke and seyde benedicite
What frere Ihn what maner world is þis  
I se wel þat sumthyng þere is amys
ȝe loke as thow þe wode were ful of thewys
Sit doun anon and telle vs what ȝoure gref is
And it schal ben amendyt If I may
I haue quod he had a dispit to day
God ȝilde ȝow adoun in ȝoure village
That in þis world nys non so poure a page
That he nulde haue abomynacioun
Of þat I hare resseyuyd in ȝoure toun
And ȝit me greuyth me no þyng so sore
As þat þis olde cherl with lokys hore
Blasfemyd hath oure holy couent ek
Now maystir quod þe lord I ȝow besek
No maystyr quod he sire but seruytour
Thow I haue had in scole þat honour
God lykyth not þat rabi men vs calle
Neyþer in market nyn in ȝoure large halle
No fors quod he but telle me al ȝoure gref
Syre quod þis frere an odyous myschef
þis day is betid to myn ordere and me
And so par concequens to eche degre
Of holy cherche god amende it sone
Syre quod þe lord ȝe wete what is to done
Distemperyth ȝow not ȝe ben myn confessour
ȝe ben þe salt of þe cherche and þe sauour
ffor godys loue ȝoure pacience ȝe holde
Telle me ȝoure gref and he anon hym tolde
As ȝe han herd before ȝe wete wel what
Te lady of þe hous ay stille sat
Til sche hadde herd what þe frere seyde
Ey godis modyr quod sche blysful mayde
Is þere not elle telle me feythfully
Madame quod he how lykyth ȝow herby
  
How þat me thynkyth quod sche so god me speede
I seye a cherl haþ don a cherlis dede
What schulde I seye god lete hym neuere the
His syke hed is ful of vanyte
I holde hym in a manere of frenesye  
Madame by god I schal not lye
But I on oþer whise may ben wreke
I schal defame hym ouyral þere I speke
This false blasfemour þat chargede me
To departe þat wele not departede be
What euery man Ilyche meche with myschaunce
The lord sat stylle as he were in a trance
And in his herte he rollede vp and doun
How hadde þis cherl þis ymaginacioun
To schewe þis probleme to a frere
Neuere erst er now herde I of swych matere
I trowe þe deuyl put it in his mynde
In arsmatryk coude þere no man fynde
Byforn þis day swich a questyoun
Who schulde mak a demonstracioun
That euery man schul haue Ilyche hise part
As of þe soun or sonour of a fart
O nyse proude cherl Ischrewe his face
Lo serys quod þe lord with harde grace
Ho herde euere of swich a thyng er now
To euery man Ilike telle me howe
It is an inpossible it may not be
Ey nyce cherl god lete hym neuere the
The rumbelyng of a fart and euery soun
Nys bot of eyr reuerberacioun
And euere it wastith lyte and lyte awey
þere is no man can deme be myn fey
ȝif þat it were departid equally
What lo myn cherl lo how schrewedely
Vp to myn confessour to day he spak
I holde hym certaynly demonyak
  
Now ete ȝoure mete and lete þe cherl go pleye
Let hym gon hangyn him selue a deuele wey
Now stod þe lordys squyer at þe bord
That karf his mete and herde word be word
Of alle thynge whiche I haue ȝow sayd
Myn lord quod he be ȝe not euele apayd
I coude telle for a goune cloth  
To ȝow sere frere be so ȝe ben not wroth
How þat þis fart schulde euene delid be
Among ȝoure couent ȝif it lyke me
Telle quod þe lord and þou schat haue anon
A gounne cloth by god and be seynt Iohn
Myn lord quod he whan þat þe wedir is fayr
Withoute wynd or parturbynge of eyr
Lat brynge a carte whel here  in to þis halle
But loke þat it haue hyse spokys alle
Twelue spokys hath a carte whel trowe I
And brynge me þanne twelve frerys wet ȝe why
ffor trettene is a couent as I gesse
The confessour here for his worthynesse
Schal parforme vp þe nombre of his couent
Thanne schul þey knele don be on asent
And to euery spokys ende in his manere
fful sadly leye his nose schal a frere
ȝoure nobele confessour þere god hym saue
Schal holde his nose vpryght vndyr þe naue
Thanne schal þis cherl with bely sterne and stout
As ony tabour ben hedyr brought out
And sette hym on þe whil ryȝt off þis carte
Vpon þe naue and make hym lete a farte
And ȝe schuln seen vp peryl of myn lyf
By pref which þat is demostratyf
  
That equally þe soun of it wele wende
And ek þe stynk vnto þe spokys ende
Saue þat þis worthy man þis confessour
By cause he is a man of gret honour
Schal han þe ferste freut as worthy is
And as þe nobele vsage ȝit of frerys is
The worthy men of hem schul ferst be servid
And serteynly he hath it wel deseruyd
He hath to day tauȝt vs so meche good
With prechynge in þe pulpit þere he stod
That I may vouche saf I sey for me
He hadde þe ferste smel of fartys thre

He berith hym so faire and holili
The Lorde the Ladie and euery man saf the ffrere
Seiden that Iankyn spak well in this matere
As well as Ouyde or Ptholome
Touchyng the cherle thei seide that subtilite
And hye witte made hym speke as he spak
He is no fooll ne no demonyak
And Iankyn hath wonne a newe gowne
Mi tale is done we ben almost at towne

Ye ride as stylle as Coy as dothe a mayde
Were newe spoused sittynge at þe borde
þis day ne herd I of youre mouthe a worde
I trowe þat ȝe study aboute some sophyme
But salamon saithe alle þenge hathe tyme
ffor goddes sake bethe of better chere
hit ys no tyme nowe to study here
Telle vs som mery tale by your fay
ffor what man ys entred in to a play
he nedes mote into þat play assent
But precheth not as freres done in lent
To make us for oure olde synnes to wepe
Ne þat þi Tale ne make vs not to slepe
Telle vs some mery þenge of auentures
ȝoure termes your figoures and your coloures
kepe hem in store tyl so be ȝe hem endite
hieȝe style as when men to kynges wryte
Spekethe so playne at þis tyme I you pray  
þat we may vndirstonde what ȝe say
This worþi Clerke benyngely vnswared
Oste quod he I am vnder your ȝerde
ȝe haue as nowe of vs þe Gouernaunce
And þerfore wolle I do ȝowe now obeysaunce
  
As fer as reson askethe hardely
I wille you telle a tale whiche þat I
lerned at Padow of a worþi clerke
As prouyd by hys wordes and his werk
he ys nowe dede and nailid in his chest
I pray to god to sende his saul gode reste
Fraunceys petrak þe laureol poet
hiȝt þis Clerk whos rethorik swete
Illumyeth alle Italy þurgh poetrye
As lynean dyd of philosophi ·
Or lawe or oþere art particuler
But dethe þat wolle suffre no þinge here
But as hit were twynkelynge of an eye
Bothe hathe he slayne and alle shalle we deye
But for to tellen of þis worthi man
þat taught me þis tale as I first began
I sey þat he first with hiȝe stile enditethe
Or he þe body of his tale writeth
A prochem in þe whiche desernethe he
The Mounde and of Saluce þe contre
And spekethe of appenen þe hilles hie
þat bene þe boundes · of west lumbardye
And of Mounte resulus in special
where as þe Pope out of a welle smal
Takith his first spryngynge and his sours
Where as he holte þe euen streight way his cours
To enel ward to Ferrar and to venyse
The whiche a longe þenge were to devise
And truly as to my Iugement
Me thynke hit a thinge impertinent
Saue he wolle conueye his matere  
But this is þe tale whiche þat ȝe shulle here
There ys at þe weste syde of Itayle
Doun at þe root of vesulus þe cold
A lusty playne habundaunt of vitayle
Where many a Toun þou mayste beholde
þat founded were in tyme of eldres old
And many an oþer delectable siȝt
And Saluce þis noble cuntre hiȝt
 A marquis whilom was in þat londe
As were his worþi eldres hym before
And obeisaunt and redy to his honde
Were alle his legees bothe lesse and more
Thus in delyte he lyued and hath done ȝore
Byloued and drad þurgh fauoure and fortune
Bothe of his lordes and of his comune
 þere with he was as to speke of lynage
þe gentelest yborne of alle lumbardy
A fayre person and stronge and yonge of age
And fulle of honour and curtesye
discrete ynouȝe his contrey for to guye
Saue in some thenges he was to blame
And Walter was þis yonge lordes name
 I blame hym þus þat he considerith nouȝt
In tyme comynge what myȝt betyde
But on his luste present was alle his þouȝt
And forto hauke and hunte on euery syde
Wele nyeȝ alle oþere cures let he slyde
And eke he ne wolde þat was worste of alle
Wedde no wyf for ouȝte þat myȝt befalle
  
‖ Only þat poynt his peple bare so sore130 

þat flok mele on a day þei went

Or ellis that the lorde wolde best assent  
þat he shulde telle hym what his peple ment
Or elles coude he wele shewe suche mater
he to þe Marquis sayd as ȝe shulle here
O noble Marquis your humanyte  
Assuresse vs and ȝeue vs hardynesse
As ofte tyme as hit ys necessite
þat we you mowe telle oure heuynesse
Accepteth lord of youre gentilnesse
þat we to you with pitous hert compleyne
And let youre Eres nouȝt my voyce disdeyne
Alle haue I nouȝt to done in þis matere
None þan an other hathe in þis place
ȝit for asmoche as ȝe my lord so dere
haue alway shewed fauoure and grace
I dare þe better aske of you a space
Of audience to shewen oure request
And ȝe my lord to done riȝt as you lust
ffor certes lord so wele vs lyketh you
And alle youre werkes and euere haue don þat we ·
Ne coude not oure owen self devisen howe
we myȝt more lyf in felicite
Safe on þenge lord yf hit youre wille be
þat for to be a wedded man ȝif þou lyst
þan were youre pepull in soueren hertes rest
Bowith ȝoure nekke  vndyr þe blysful ȝok  
Of souereynte  and not of seruyse
Which þat men clepe  sponsayle or wedlok
And thynkith lord  among ȝoure thouȝtys wyse
  
How þat oure dayis  passe in sundery wyse
ffor thow we slepe  or wake or rome or ryde
Ay fleth þe tyme  it nyl no man abyde
And þow ȝoure  grene thouȝt floure as ȝit
In crepith age  alwey as stylle as ston
And deth manasith  euery age and smyt
In eche estat  for þere escapith noon
And also serteyn  as we knowyn echon
That we schal deye  as vncerteyn with alle
Been of þat day  whan deth schal on vs falle
Acceptyth þanne  of vs þe trewe entent
That neuere ȝit  refusedyn þyn heste
And we wele lord  ȝif þat ȝe wele assent
Chese ȝow a wyf  in schort tyme at þe leste
Born of þe  gentilleste and of þe meste
Of al þis lond  so þat it oghte seene
Honour to god  and ȝow as we can deme
Delyuere vs  out of al þis bosy drede
And tak a wif for hyghe godis sake
ffor ȝif it  so befel as god forbede
That þorw ȝoure deth ȝoure lyf schulde slake
And þat a straunge successour schulde take
ȝoure erytage o wo were vs on lyue
Wherfore we prey ȝow hastyly to wyue
Hire meke preyere and here pitous chire
Made þe Markis herte to haue pytee
ȝe wele quod he myn owene peple dere
To þat I neuere erst thouȝte to streyne me
I me reioysede of myn libertee
That selde tyme is founde in maryage
There I was fre I mote been in seruage
  
But na the les I se ȝoure trewe entent  
And truste vpon ȝoure wit and han don ay
Werfore of myn fre wil I wele assente
To wedde me as sone as euere I may
But þere as ȝe han proferede me to day
To chese me a wyf I ȝow relese
That choys and prey ȝow of þat profere sese
Let me alone In chesynge of myn wyf
That charge vpon myn bak I wele endure
But I ȝow preye and charge vpon ȝoure lyf
What wyf þat I take I ȝow ensure
To worschepe hire whil þat hyre lyf may dure
In word and werk bothe here and ellis where
As sche an emperourys douȝtir were
ffor god it wot þat childeryn oftyn been
Vnlyk here worthy elderys hem before
Bounte comyth of god  nat of þe treen
Of whiche þey been engenderede and Ibore
I truste in goddis bounte and þerfore
Myn maryage and myn estat and resste
I hym betake  he may don as hym leste
And ferþere more þis schal ȝe swere þat ȝe
Ageyn myn choys schul neyþer groche ne striue
ffor sythe I schal forgon myn lyberte
At ȝoure request as euere mote i thryue
There as myn herte is set þere wele I wyue
And but ȝe wele asente in swych manere
I prey ȝow spekyth no mor of þis mateere
With hertely wil þey swore and asentyn
To al þis thyng þere sey no wigh nay
Besekynge hym of grace er þat þey wente
That he wolde grauntyn hem a serteyn day
  
Of his sponsayle as sone as euere he may
ffor ȝit alwey þe puple sumwhat dredde
Lest þat þe markes no wyf wolde wedde
He grauntede hem a day swych as hym leste  
On which he wolde be weddit sekyrly
And seyde he dede al þis at his requeste
And þey with humble entent buxsomly
Knelynge vpon hire kneis ful reuerently
Hym thankede alle and þus þey han an ende
Of hire entent and hom ageyn þey wende
And here vp on he to hise offyserys
Comaundith for þe feste to purueye
And to hyse priue knyȝtis and squyerys
Swich charge ȝaf as hym leste on hem leye
And þey to hise comandementis obeye
And ech of hem doth al his dilygence
To don vnto þe feste reuerence
 Oght fer from thilke paleys honurable
Where as þis Markys  schop his maryage
Ther was a thorpt of sighte delytable
In which þat poore folk of þat village
Haddyn here bestis and here herbergage
And of hire labour tok here sustenaunce
Aftyr þat þe erþe  ȝaf hem habundaunce
Amongys þese poore  folk þere dwellede a man
Whiche þat was holde  poreste of hem alle
But highe god  sumtyme sende can
His grace into  a lytyl oysis stalle
Ianicula  men of þat thorp hym calle
A doughtyr he hadde  fayr and ȝyng to syȝte
And Grysilde  þis ȝynge maydyn hyȝte
  
But for to speke  of verteuous beute
Thanne was sche on  þe fayreste vndyr sunne
ffor pourely  Ifosterede vp was sche
No lykerous lust  was thorw hire herte Ironne
Weel oftere of  þe welle þan of þe tunne
Sche drank and for  sche wolde vertu plese
Sche knew wel labour  but non ydyl ese
But thow þis mayd  tendere was of age  
ȝit in þe 1in here chaste virginite1
There was enclosede rype and sad corage
And in gret  reuerence and charyte
Hyre olde pore  fadyr fosterede sche
A fewe schep  spynnynge on feld sche kepte
Sche wolde not  ben ydyl tyl sche slepte
And whan sche homward  cam sche wolde brynge
Wortis or oþere  erbis tymys ofte
The whiche sche dalf  and sette for hyre lyuynge
And made hyre bed  ful harde and nothyng softe
And ay sche kepte hyre faderys lyf on lofte
With euery obeysaunce and dilygence
That child may don to  faders reuerence
Vpon Grysilde  þis pore creature
fful ofte tyme  þis Markis sette his eye
As he an huntyng  rod parauenture
And whan it fel  þat he myȝte hire espye
He not with wauntoun  lokyng of folye
His eyen cast on  here  but in sad wyse
Vpon hire cher  he wolde hym ofte avyse
Comendynge in his  herte  hire womanhede
And ek hire verteus  passynge ony wyght
Of so ȝyng age  as wel in chere as dede
ffor thogh þe puple  hath no gret ensyȝt
  
In vertu he  consyderede ful ryȝt
Hire bouteis  and purposede þat he wolde
Wedde hire only  ȝif þat he wedde schulde
The day of weddyng  cam but no wight kan
Telle what  woman þat it schulde be
ffor whiche merueyle  wonderede manye a man
And seydyn whan þat  þey were in pryuyte
Wele not oure lord  ȝit leue his vanyte
Wele he not wedde  allas allas þe whyle
Whi wele he þus hym self and vs begyle
But natheles þis Markis hath don make  
Of gounnys set  in gold and in asure
Brochis and ryngis  for gresildis sake
And of hire clothynge  tok he þe mesure
By a maydyn  lyk to hyr stature
And ek of oþere  aornementis alle
That on to swich  a weddyng schulde falle
The tyme of vnderne  of þe soneday
Aprochith that  þis weddynge schulde bee
And al þe paleys  put was In aray
Bothe halle and chaumberys  eche in hese degre
Housis of offysis  stuffed with gret plente
There mayst þou sen  of deynteuous vitayle
That may be founde  as fer as last ytaylle
This riche Markis  ryally arayed
Lordis and ladiis in his cumpaynye
The whech to þe  feste were Ipreyed
And of his  retente þe bacherye
And manye a soun  of sundery melodye
Vnto þe village  of þe whiche I tolde
In þis aray  þe ryȝte weye han holde
  
Gresylde of þis  god wot ful Innocent
That for hire schapyn  was al þis aray
To feche watyr  at a welle is went
And comyth hom  as sone as euere sche may
ffor wel sche hadde  herd seyd þat ilke day
The Markys schulde  wedde and ȝif sche myȝt
Sche wolde fayn  a seyn sum of þat syȝte
Sche thouȝte sche wolde  with oþere maydenys stonde
That been myne felas  in oure dore and see
The Mayrkysesse  and þerfore wele I fonde
To doon at hom  as sone as it may bee
The labour which  þat longith on to me
And þanne I may  at  leysere hire byholde
ȝif sche this weye  vnto þe castel holde
And as sche wolde  ouyr hyre throswald gon  
The Markis cam  and gan hyre for to calle
And sche sette doun  hyre watyr pot anon
By syde þe throschewald  in an oxis stalle
And doun vpon hyre  kneis sche gan to falle
And with sad cuntenaunce  knelede stylle
Til sche hadde  herd þe lordis wille
This thoghtful Markys  spak vnto þis mayde
fful sobirly  and seyth  in þis manere
Where is ȝoure fadyr  O Grysild he seyde
And sche with reuerence  In humble chere
Answerde lord  he is al redy here
And in sche goth  sche 1wolde no lengere lette1
And to þe Markis  sche hyre fadyr fette
He by the hond  thanne tok þis olde man
And seyde þus  whan he hym hadde a syde
Ianicula  I neyþer may ne kan
Lengere þe plesaunce  of myn herte hyde
  
ȝif þat þou vouche saf what so betyde
Thyn douȝtyr wele I  take 1er þan I wende1
As for myn wif  vnto myn lyuys ende
Thow louyst me  I wot it wel serteyn
And art myn feythful  lyge man Ibore
And al þat lykyth me  I dare wel seyn
It lykyth þe  and specially þerfore
Tel me þat poynt  þat I haue seyd before
ȝif that þou wilt  vnto þat purpos drawe
To take me  as for þyn sone in lawe
The sodeyn cas  þis man astonede so
That red he wex  abayst and al quakynge
He stod oneþe  seyde he wordys moo
But only this  lord quod he myn willyng
Is as ȝe wele  ne aȝens ȝoure lykyng
I wele no thyng  ȝe be myn lord so dere
Ryght as ȝow lyst  gouernyth þis matyere
That wel I wot  quod  þis Markis softely  
That in thy chambir  I and þou and sche
Haue a colacioun  and wyst þou whi
ffor I wele aske ȝif it hire wille be
To be myn wif  and rewele hyr aftyr me
And al þis schal been don  in þyn presence
I wele not spek  out of þyn audience
And in þe chambere  whil þey were aboute
This tretys which  þat ȝe schul aftyr here
The puple cam  vnto þe hous withoute
And wondere hem  in how oneste manere
And tentyfli sche  kepte hire fadyr dere
But outyrly  Grisildis wondere myghte
ffor neuere erst  ne saw sche swich a syghte
  
No wondir ist  þow þat sche were astonyd
To seen so greet  a geste come into plase
Sche neuere was  to swich a geste wonyd
ffor whiche sche lokede  with ful pale face
But schortly þis  matyer for to chase
These are þe wordis  þat þe Markis sayde
To þis benynge  veray feyhful mayde
Grysilde he seyde  ȝe schul wel vndyrstonde
It lykyt to ȝoure  fadyr and to me
That I ȝow wedde  and ek it may so stonde
As I suppose  ȝe wele þat it so be
But þese demaundis  aske I ferst quod he
That sythe it schal  been don in hasty wyse
Wele ȝe assentyn  or ellis ȝow auyse
I seye þis be ȝe  redy with good herte
To al myn lust  and þat I frely may
As me best lykyth  do ȝow lauhe or smerte
And neuere ȝe  to groche it nyght ne day
And ek whan I seye ȝa  ne seye not nay
Neyther be word  ne frounnynge cuntenaunce
Swere þis  and here I swere oure allyaunce
Wonderynge vpon þis word quakynge for drede  
Sche seyde lord  vndyng and vnworthy
I am to thilke honour þat ȝe me beede
But as ȝe wele ȝoure self ryȝt so wele I
And here I swere  þat neuere wyllyngly
In werk ne thouȝt I nyl ȝow disobeye
ffo to be ded thow me were loth to dye
Tis is Inogh Grysilde myn quod he
And forth he goth with a ful noble cheere
Out at þe dore and aftyr þat cam sche
And to þe puple he seyde in þis manere
  
This is myn wif  quod he þat standyth heere
Honoureth hire  and louyth hire I preye
Who so me louyth þere is no more to seye
And for þat nothyng  of hire olde gere
Sche schulde brynge into his hous he bad
That wemen schulde dispoylyn hire ryȝt þere
Of whiche þese  ladyis were not ryȝt glad
To handele hire clothis  wherIn sche was clad
But natheles þis mayde bryȝt of hewe
ffrom foot to heed they cloþede han al newe
Hyre heris han þey kembit that lay vntrussede
fful rudely and with here fyngerys smale
A coroun on hire heed þey han dressyd
And set hire ful of nouchis grete and smale
Of hire aray what schulde I make a tale
Oneþe þe puple hire knew for hire fayrnesse
Whan sche translatede was in swich rychesse
This Markis hath hire spousede with a ryng
Brouȝt for þe same cause and þanne hire sette
Vpon an hors snow whit and wel amblenge
And to his paleys he wolde no lengere lette
With Ioyful puple þat hire ledde and mette
Conueyede hire and þus þe day þey spende
In reuel tyl þe sonne gan descende
And shortely forth þis tale for to chace  
I seye þat to þis  newe Markysesse
God hath swych fauour sent hire of his grace
That it semede not bi liklynesse
That sche was born and fed in rewedenesse
As in a Cote  or in an oxsis stalle
But norchede in  an emperourys halle
  
To euery wight sche wexen is so dere
And worchepeful  þat folk þere sche was bore
And from hyre burthe knew hire ȝer be ȝere
Oneþe trowede þey but durste a swore
That to Ianykele of which I spak before
Sche doghtir were  for as be coniecture
